# Feature Optimization

> This file tracks ways to REFINE features that already exist in this project.
> It is NOT a roadmap of new features to add — nothing here introduces new
> functionality. Every item makes an existing feature cleaner, faster, safer,
> more accessible, or otherwise better.
>
> Maintained by the `/optimize-features` command. Last full inventory: 2026-07-19

## Feature Inventory

### A. Portal shell & navigation

| # | Feature | What it does | Where it lives | Last reviewed |
|---|---------|--------------|----------------|---------------|
| 1 | Welcome page & section catalog | "Instrument" redesign (PRs #169/#170): cinematic framed hero (`WelcomeHero` + volumetric fog field, floating curriculum-constellation nodes), glass pill nav branded Quantum Learner with the atom mark, warm account band, feature bands, dual auth CTAs, live playground stat; curriculum grid behind a sign-up gate modal; catalog + progress derive from the content manifest | `web/src/app/page.tsx`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx`, `web/src/components/{fog-field,nav,curriculum-grid,section-gate-modal}.tsx`, `web/src/lib/{sections,section-pitch}.ts` | 2026-07-19 |
| 2 | Lesson reader | Static-export page per section: renders GUIDE.md via react-markdown and routes ~30 fenced code blocks to interactive widgets at build time | `web/src/app/learn/[section]/page.tsx`, `web/src/components/markdown-renderer.tsx`, `web/src/lib/content.ts` | 2026-07-03 |
| 3 | In-lesson navigation | Sidebar, prev/next links, animated page transitions, and a table of contents kept in lockstep with rendered heading ids | `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx`, `prev-next.tsx`, `transition-link.tsx`, `table-of-contents.tsx`, `web/src/lib/extract-headings.ts` | 2026-07-03 |
| 4 | Dark / light theme & design tokens | Theme toggle backed by next-themes, with compile-time tokens via Tailwind v4 `@theme inline`; site-wide "Instrument" token system (PR #169): theme-aware olive accent as a runtime var, glass + glass-shadow surfaces, Sora/Geist/Geist Mono type, tan→olive data-bar gradient, motion keyframes — all reduced-motion safe, both themes | `web/src/components/theme-toggle.tsx`, `web/src/app/globals.css`, `web/src/app/layout.tsx` | 2026-07-19 |
| 5 | Progress tracking | Per-section completion state in localStorage, surfaced as catalog progress and a nav badge, via SSR-safe `useSyncExternalStore` | `web/src/lib/progress-store.ts`, `web/src/hooks/use-progress.ts`, `web/src/components/section-progress.tsx` | 2026-07-03 |

### I. Workspace & accounts

> New category — the project gained an authenticated Workspace surface (PRs #76/#77). Numbers are append-only identifiers (the Optimization Opportunities section references `### N`), so categories I–J are listed after H even though they are user-facing and conceptually sit nearer A–D.

| # | Feature | What it does | Where it lives | Last reviewed |
|---|---------|--------------|----------------|---------------|
| 34 | Quantum Workspace authentication | AWS Cognito login for the Workspace: email/password sign-up, email-code confirm, sign-in, password reset, and Google federated OAuth, with eyeball show/hide + live password-criteria checklist + confirm-field gating; env-gated on four `NEXT_PUBLIC_COGNITO_*`/region vars (UI shows "coming soon" when unset). NOW A PLATFORM-WIDE SIGN-UP WALL (`a72b705`, branch `feat/signup-wall-drop-grant`): layout-mounted `AuthWall` gates every product route (only `/`, `/pricing`, `/privacy` + auth routes public), redirects to `/login?next=<path>` (same-origin only), inert without Cognito env. `/workspace` grew into the bench (Feature 39); cross-device backend sync shipped (Feature 38) | `web/src/app/{login,auth/callback,workspace}/page.tsx`, `web/src/components/auth/*` (incl. `auth-wall.tsx`), `web/src/lib/{auth-config,auth-errors,password-policy}.ts`, `infra/workspace/cognito.yaml` | 2026-07-19 |

## Optimization Opportunities

> **2026-07-19 reconciliation pass.** All 47 features re-verified present (route surface
> unchanged: 12 top-level app routes + `/learn/[section]`, `/glossary/[term]`,
> `/auth/callback`, `/e2e-fixtures`). No capability added or removed — the count holds
> at **47**. Since 2026-07-17, three changes landed, all refinements of existing rows:
> **PR #169** (Instrument redesign — site-wide smoke-and-glass token system, cinematic
> `WelcomeHero` + fog field, glass pill nav, branded OG card; rows 1/4/36 updated),
> **PR #170** (nav rebranded Quantum Learner + atom mark, warm account band, brighter
> hero constellation; row 1), and **`a72b705`** on branch `feat/signup-wall-drop-grant`
> (NOT yet merged to main): a platform-wide sign-up wall via a layout-mounted `AuthWall`
> — only `/`, `/pricing`, `/privacy` + auth routes public, everything else gates to
> `/login?next=<path>` — plus removal of the display-only 500-credit welcome grant
> (rows 34/36/44 updated). `Last reviewed` bumped on the six touched rows; deep
> findings below retain their original dates.
>
> **2026-07-19 Category A Phase-3 re-audit** (the A-to-N full-inventory campaign, phase 1 of 14):
> a 117-agent workflow (5 features x 3 lens-group finders + 5 completeness critics, then one
> adversarial verifier per candidate) produced 100 candidates -> 96 confirmed -> **86 recorded**
> after cross-feature merge (10 duplicate reports of 7 shared root causes folded into canonical
> copies with cross-refs). New unchecked items sit under ### 1-### 5, High first: 9 High /
> 39 Medium / 38 Low. Standouts: signed-out prospects bounced to a contextless sign-in by the
> new wall's redirect (no mode=signup, welcome-band CTAs skip the gate modal), no site nav below
> 768px, the closed mobile drawer's 7 links left in the tab order, wide tables/KaTeX forcing
> body-level horizontal scroll at 375px, the light-theme focus ring at 1.60:1, and a token-contrast
> test gap where one #169 WCAG comment is already false.

> **2026-07-17 inventory refresh + notebook-loop analysis.** Since 2026-07-03, PRs #90–#164
> shipped **eleven new features** — the inventory grows 36 → **47** (categories K–N added):
> the graded-Rep widget family + mastery loop (through #98), cross-device progress sync,
> the workspace bench (#141/#144), Runbook & Credentials (#151), review-email reminders +
> `/privacy` (#134), the playground sandbox (#145/#147), the sponsored QPU track (#119–#146),
> the pricing page (#162), Stripe billing & wallet (#163/#164), the CI warm-standby mirror
> (#149), and the quantumlearner.dev redirect (#103). Rows 1/13/15/16/17/34 were updated to
> current reality — notably **row 17 is corrected**: `quiz` blocks are reveal-answer
> self-checks, not graded multiple-choice (`quiz.tsx` computes no verdict and persists
> nothing). The refinement-roadmap premise "a grader computes a verdict but never calls
> gradeCard()" **closed in PR #98** — all six graded Rep kinds now feed `gradeCardIfDue`
> (`challenge.tsx:138` and siblings). This run's Phase-3 pass (3-agent ground-truth read)
> analyzed the **notebook exercise loop** — TODO hints that steer without revealing, a real
> grader for exercise responses, per-user score tracking — with new findings under `### 27`,
> `### 15`, `### 37`, and a boundary note under `### 13-14`.
>
> **2026-07-17 execution.** All five of those findings SHIPPED as a 3-PR train, all merged
> and Amplify-deployed: **#165** (`83b8570`) closed the three `### 27` items — 44 notebooks
> converted to the tiered-hint + `# Check Exercise N` convention (`docs/exercise-convention.md`,
> `lib/grading.py`), with `tests/test_exercise_checks.py` proving every check passes with its
> canonical answer and fails unsolved (146 tests in `make test`). **#166** (`ac1db0e`) closed
> the `### 37` solved-flag item via the shared `usePersistentSolved` hook. **#167** (`c637988`)
> closed the `### 15` py-tier item — grading-integrity fix, an e2e-coverage allowlist, 4 shipped
> `tier:"py"` Reps, and Playwright proof. The `### 13-14` lab-bridge note stays a boundary
> (out of scope), addressed instead by the py-tier rail.

> **2026-07-03 reconciliation pass.** All 36 features re-verified present against `main` —
> every inventory path resolves (67 spot-checked paths, the 63 `web/src/components/quantum/*`
> widgets, the six `web/src/components/auth/*` files, the seven curriculum sections), no
> capability added or removed, so the count holds at **36**. Since 2026-06-29, **PRs #82–#89**
> merged — all refinements, no new features: the Category E (`lib/`) series shipped as
> #82 (the four Mediums), #83 (cost subsystem), #84 (utils tail), #85 (hardware tail),
> #86 (QML residual), #87 (P1 — Feature 21 + cross-cutting), #88 (P2 — Feature 22 chemistry),
> and #89 closed the tutor ops tail (preflight deploy gate + stack-managed log retention).
> Every Category E item below still annotated "DONE (PR pending)" is now **merged** via that
> series — this note is the resolution record; per-item annotations were left as written.
> This pass **closed one open item** (19-20 [Tests/Ops], see below) and **sharpened the two
> remaining `### 22-23` items** to their still-open halves. `Last reviewed` bumped to

> These refined existing features; three of them closed open optimization items below, now

> **2026-07-19 Phase-3 re-audit (Category A workflow: 117 agents, findings adversarially verified one-by-one).**
> This surface is almost entirely new since the 2026-06-17 pass (#148/#150/#169/#170). 23 verified findings, High first.

- [x] **[UX]** Welcome page's playground/runbook/nav links bounce signed-out prospects to a contextless sign-in view — The welcome page is the conversion surface, but only the curriculum cards got the thoughtful sign-up gate (per-section preview modal with pitch and 'Create a free account'). The equally prominent band CTAs 'Open the playground' and 'Read the hardware runbook', plus the nav pill's Playground/Runbook/Credentials links, point at routes behind the new AuthWall: a signed-out visitor who clicks them sees a flash of the 'Checking your access…' spinner and is replaced onto /login — in the SIGN-IN view, because the wall's redirect never carries mode=signup, and with zero copy explaining why they were bounced. A brand-new prospect (the majority of welcome-page traffic) must then find the 'Create account' toggle themselves. The same page proves the better pattern exists one scroll below. _Fix:_ Make the welcome surface's gating consistent: for signed-out sessions, intercept plain clicks on the page's protected-destination links the same way CurriculumGrid already does (reuse the existing modal affordance with the band's own pitch copy), or at minimum have those links / the AuthWall redirect carry mode=signup plus next=…, so a prospect clicking 'Open the playground' lands on 'Create your account' with their destination preserved rather than an unexplained 'Sign in' form. No new capability — this extends the gate pattern the page already ships to the rest of its links. Impact: High. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/app/page.tsx:137-148`, `web/src/components/auth/auth-wall.tsx:14`, `web/src/components/auth/auth-wall.tsx:58-62`, `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:28`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UX]** No site navigation below 768px — the glass pill simply disappears with no mobile affordance — The centered glass pill (Playground, Runbook, Credentials, Pricing) is `hidden … md:flex` and there is no hamburger, disclosure, or wrapped row to replace it. At 375px the header offers only the brand link, Review, Sign in, and the theme toggle; reaching Playground, Runbook, Credentials — or Pricing, a public funnel page — requires scrolling past the entire welcome page (or any other page) to the footer. Every mobile visitor on every route loses primary navigation, and on the welcome page specifically the pricing funnel is invisible from the header. _Fix:_ Surface the existing four pill links below md within the current header idiom — e.g. let the pill wrap onto a second compact row under the h-16 bar on small screens, or render it as a horizontally scrollable chip row — keeping the same rounded-chip/glass-2 styling and link set. Pure responsive correction of the existing nav; no new destinations or components beyond the disclosure of what already exists. Impact: High. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/nav.tsx:44`, `web/src/components/footer.tsx:19-36`, `web/src/components/nav.tsx:21`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Architecture]** SectionGateModal adds the repo's third hand-rolled focus trap, and the three FOCUSABLE selectors have already drifted apart — The gate modal reimplements the Tab-cycle focus trap that sidebar.tsx and ask-tutor.tsx each already carry. All three copies have the same first/last/shiftKey wrap logic but three different focusable-element selectors: the gate modal omits input/textarea entirely, the sidebar adds input:not([disabled]), and ask-tutor includes raw `textarea, input` without the :not([disabled]) guard. Accessibility-critical logic is triplicated and silently diverging - the next dialog (or the next form control added to any of these three) inherits whichever variant its author copies. _Fix:_ Extract one shared focus-trap into web/src/hooks (e.g. use-focus-trap.ts exporting the canonical FOCUSABLE selector and a keydown handler/hook over a container ref) and adopt it in all three dialogs. Behavior-preserving refactor; the existing sidebar.test.tsx, ask-tutor.test.tsx, and curriculum-grid.test.tsx focus/keyboard suites verify parity for free. _Cross-feature: the F3 audit independently flagged the same triplication from the sidebar side - one shared hook closes both._ Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/section-gate-modal.tsx:28-29,75-91`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:97-117`, `web/src/components/ask-tutor.tsx:160-180`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Performance]** FogField rasterizes 5-10 full-viewport radial gradients every frame, on every route, with no sprite cache and no delta-time — The site-wide ambient canvas re-creates a CanvasGradient object and gradient-fills a circle of up to 580px radius for each of 5-10 blobs on every animation frame, forever, at up to 2x DPR. Gradient fills are among the most expensive 2D-canvas operations; this is continuous paint work and GC churn on every page of the platform (lessons, playground, review), not just the welcome page. Additionally blob positions advance a fixed amount per frame (p.x += p.vx) with no timestamp delta, so on 120 Hz displays the fog drifts twice as fast and burns twice the paint work as on 60 Hz. _Fix:_ At seed() time, pre-render each blob's gradient once into a small offscreen canvas sprite (one per palette color/radius), then in draw() composite with ctx.globalAlpha = a and drawImage(sprite, ...) — identical visuals, but per-frame work drops from gradient rasterization to cached-bitmap blits. While there, scale movement by the rAF timestamp delta (velocities per ms) so drift speed and energy cost are identical on 60 Hz and 120 Hz displays. No new dependencies; same file, same visual output. _Cross-feature: the F4 audit independently flagged the same loop (FogField is mounted site-wide) - one fix._ Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:99`, `web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:93-94`, `web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:113`, `web/src/app/layout.tsx:68`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UX]** GlossaryCard sits in the gated grid but bypasses the gate — same list, two signed-out behaviors — Within the one role=list curriculum grid, signed-out clicks on the seven section cards are intercepted in place by the polished preview dialog with account CTAs, while a click on the adjacent GlossaryCard (same chrome, same hover language) hard-navigates into the AuthWall, which yanks the visitor off the marketing page to the bare /login form (/glossary is not in PUBLIC_PATHS). Distinct from the auditors' nav-link finding: the defect locus is the grid itself — CurriculumGrid already owns gate machinery and applies it to only one of its two card types, so identical-looking siblings behave differently for the exact same visitor. _Fix:_ Unify the signed-out treatment inside CurriculumGrid using machinery it already has: intercept the glossary click with the same modal pattern (the dialog already handles a pitch + CTA layout; the glossary needs only its existing card copy and a next=/glossary on the CTAs), or at minimum route the card through /login?mode=signup&next=/glossary so the bounce keeps sign-up framing and destination. Extend curriculum-grid.test.tsx, which currently never clicks the glossary card while signed out. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/curriculum-grid.tsx:34-67`, `web/src/components/glossary-card.tsx:9-13`, `web/src/components/auth/auth-wall.tsx:14,56-62`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Cleaner code]** AI tutor band hand-copies the entire feature-band scaffolding instead of flowing through the bands array — page.tsx renders three feature bands from the FeatureBand[] array, then re-implements the identical two-column band markup inline for the AI tutor band (~70 lines) because FeatureBand only supports an image visual. The kicker &lt;p&gt;, display-lg &lt;h3&gt;, body &lt;p&gt;, arrow link, and the arrow SVG path are duplicated verbatim, so any band-styling change must be made twice on the repo's highest-churn page (rewritten three times since PR #148); HomePage is 466 lines. _Fix:_ Widen FeatureBand to carry `visual: ReactNode` (the three photo bands pass the framed &lt;img&gt;, the tutor band passes the Ask-the-margin mock), extract a small Band component plus the tutor mock panel into web/src/components/welcome/ (the folder PR #169 already created for this surface), and render all four bands through one map. Pure markup consolidation - no behavior or copy change; home-page.test.tsx assertions keep passing untouched. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/page.tsx:81-89`, `web/src/app/page.tsx:234-281`, `web/src/app/page.tsx:287-355`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Hero decorative chrome leaks into the screen-reader stream: constellation nodes, horizons widget, '01 / 03' link name, and double-announced stats — Four pieces of purely visual hero chrome are exposed to assistive tech. (1) The four floating constellation nodes are pointer-events-none but not aria-hidden, so on lg+ a screen reader hits stray fragments ('Foundations', '12 notebooks', …) BEFORE the page's h1, since they precede the content block in DOM order. (2) The 'Quantum horizons' widget is select-none but not aria-hidden — it reads as a meaningless label plus seven empty spans. (3) The scroll-cue link's accessible name is '01 / 03 · Scroll down', announcing a decorative fake counter as if it were pagination. (4) Each hero stat renders an sr-only &lt;dt&gt; label AND a visible &lt;dd&gt; repeat of the same label, so every stat is announced twice ('curriculum sections, 7, curriculum sections'). The curriculum grid below carries the real, properly structured versions of all this information. _Fix:_ aria-hidden="true" on the node layer wrapper and the horizons widget; give the scroll cue a truthful name (aria-label="Scroll to the curriculum" with the '01 / 03' counter in an aria-hidden span); and collapse the stat duplication by dropping the sr-only dt and making the visible label the dt (or aria-hidden-ing the visible label dd). All markup-only changes to existing elements. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:43`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:168-176`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:157-164`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:143-150`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Powered-by label fails AA contrast (≈2.6:1) and the dim H1 half rides the 3:1 large-text line over a variable photo ground — In the always-dark powered-by strip, the 'Powered by' kicker is text-white/30 at 11px on the #0b0b0c ground — white at 30% alpha composites to ≈rgb(84,84,85), a contrast of ≈2.6:1 against a 4.5:1 requirement for text that size. In the hero, the second headline half ('from first principles') is text-white/35, ≈3.1:1 against the darkest possible ground — already at the 3:1 large-text floor — and it sits over the hero-fog photograph whose light bloom brightens the ground locally (the legibility wash is deliberately transparent toward the top-right, radial-gradient starting transparent at 78% -10%), pushing the effective contrast below 3:1 wherever the fog glows behind the text. These render identically in both app themes since both bands are self-dark islands, so there is no compliant theme fallback. _Fix:_ Raise the two failing/marginal alphas while keeping the intended hierarchy: 'Powered by' from white/30 to at least white/55 (≈5.8:1 at 11px), and the dim headline span from white/35 to ≈white/50 so it clears 3:1 with margin even over the bloom. Two class-token changes; the partner names at white/45 (≈4.5:1 borderline at 14px, page.tsx:210) deserve the same one-step bump for safety. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/page.tsx:206-208`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:135-137`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:97`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** FogField fully re-randomizes on every resize, so mobile URL-bar height jitter makes the fog visibly pop while scrolling — The debounced resize handler calls seed(), which re-randomizes the position, radius, velocity, and phase of every blob and speck and resets the canvas bitmap. On iOS Safari and Android Chrome, window.innerHeight changes every time the browser toolbar collapses or expands during normal scrolling, firing resize — so 180ms after a scroll direction change the entire ambient field discontinuously jumps to a new random layout behind the content. This is a visible glitch on every mobile visit, on every route. _Fix:_ In onResize, early-return when window.innerWidth === W (the toolbar-collapse case only changes height), or better: split seed() so resize re-scales existing blob coordinates to the new dimensions (x *= newW/oldW etc.) instead of re-randomizing, keeping the field continuous. Reserve full re-randomization for the initial mount and theme flips. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:120-126`, `web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:62-74`, `web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:53-57`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** Hero constellation is keyed to four hardcoded manifest slugs with a silent-drop filter and zero test assertions — The floating constellation nodes — the hero's signature element — are built by filtering manifest sections against a hardcoded slug map; any slug that no longer matches is silently dropped, and home-page.test.tsx (read in full) never asserts a single node label or count. This repo has already renumbered/renamed section directories once (the 00-06 renumber campaign), so a future manifest rename would silently empty or unbalance the flagship hero with every test green. The adjacent 'Quantum horizons' strip hardcodes 1+6=7 bars rather than deriving from sections.length, so an added section 07 would make it silently lie. _Fix:_ Add a home-page test that asserts all four constellation labels render with their manifest-derived '&lt;n&gt; notebooks' values (they are in the jsdom DOM despite the lg:block class), pinning NODE_LABELS to the live manifest so a slug rename fails loudly. Pass sections.length (already computed in page.tsx) into WelcomeHero for the horizons strip count instead of the literal 6. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/page.tsx:113-121`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:79-82`, `web/src/components/welcome/hero.tsx:171-174`, `web/__tests__/app/home-page.test.tsx:66-195`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Consistency]** Home page's openGraph override strips og:site_name and the structured OG image every other route ships — layout.tsx defines a structured OG_IMAGE (url/width/height/alt) plus openGraph.siteName as the site-wide default, but page.tsx re-declares openGraph with images: ["/og.png"] as a bare string. Next.js replaces — never deep-merges — a page-level openGraph object, so the single most-shared URL on the site is the only route missing og:site_name, og:image:width, og:image:height, and og:image:alt (which scrapers like LinkedIn/Slack use for card layout and which carries the share image's accessible description). The home test only asserts the images array contains "/og.png", so the regression is green. _Fix:_ Export the OG_IMAGE constant (and siteName string) from a shared module (e.g. web/src/lib/site.ts next to SITE_URL), and have page.tsx spread it into its openGraph: { ...{title, description, url, type}, siteName, images: [OG_IMAGE] } — one source of truth, no page-level downgrades. Tighten home-page.test.tsx to assert the image entry keeps width/height/alt. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/page.tsx:19-31`, `web/src/app/layout.tsx:40-59`, `web/__tests__/app/home-page.test.tsx:62-63`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UI]** The brand reads three different names in one viewport: Quantum Learner, Quantum Computing Workspace, Quantum Workspace — PR #170's rebrand stopped at the nav. On a single load of the welcome page the header says "Quantum Learner", the browser tab / og:site_name / OG image alt / HOME_TITLE say "Quantum Computing Workspace", and the footer says "Quantum Workspace" (the unconfigured login card adds a fourth variant, "The Quantum Workspace"). - [x] **[Resilience & tests]** FogField has zero unit coverage — its reduced-motion single-frame contract and teardown are unpinned — fog-field.tsx is a key file of this feature and the only component on the surface with no test file at all (web/__tests__/components/ contains no fog-field test). Its most important behaviors are exactly the kind that regress silently: under prefers-reduced-motion it must render one static frame and never reschedule rAF (a house rule); on unmount it must cancel the rAF, clear the resize timer, remove the listener, and disconnect the MutationObserver; and a theme flip must reseed the palette. A refactor breaking any of these produces no visible test failure — an infinite animation loop for motion-sensitive users or a leaked rAF loop after navigation would ship green. _Fix:_ Add web/__tests__/components/fog-field.test.tsx using the existing matchMedia mock pattern plus a stubbed canvas.getContext('2d') object and jest-mocked requestAnimationFrame: assert (1) with reduce matched, draw runs exactly once and rAF is not rescheduled; (2) unmount calls cancelAnimationFrame, removeEventListener('resize'), and observer.disconnect; (3) flipping the documentElement 'dark' class triggers a reseed. No new dependencies — a hand-rolled ctx stub suffices since the component only calls a dozen ctx methods. Impact: Low. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:26,113`, `web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:140-145`, `web/__tests__/components/transition-link.test.tsx:41-63`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)

- [x] **[Consistency]** The Instrument ground colors #0b0b0c and #080c14 are hardcoded hex in eight places across three files instead of design tokens — The redesign's two pinned dark grounds - the smoke frame (#0b0b0c) and the media/backdrop navy (#080c14) - are repeated as arbitrary-value literals across hero.tsx, page.tsx, and section-gate-modal.tsx, while every other surface color in the design system lives as a token (--surface-base, --glass, --bd, --shadow-*) in globals.css. - [x] **[Architecture]** Hero constellation and horizons decoration rely on cross-file positional agreements and hardcoded curriculum counts — The label-to-glyph-to-corner pairing of the four constellation nodes is implicit in index ordering split across two files: page.tsx assigns corners by array position over a slug filter, and hero.tsx assigns glyphs by the same position (glyphOrder[i % 4]). - [x] **[Performance]** og.png is a 459 KB PNG of photographic content — the wrong codec at ~4-6x the necessary weight — The branded social card referenced by every route's metadata is a 1200x630 PNG weighing 459 KB. The Instrument card art is photographic smoke-and-glass imagery, which PNG compresses terribly; every link unfurl (Slack, iMessage, LinkedIn, X) fetches this file, and slow or size-budgeted crawlers render previews late or degrade them. My lens brief explicitly names this asset. _Fix:_ Recompress the existing art: export as quality ~80 JPEG (typically 60-120 KB for this kind of imagery, and JPEG is universally supported by unfurlers) or run pngquant if PNG must stay; keep 1200x630 and the same /og.png path so no code changes. - [x] **[UI]** Wide GUIDE tables and display equations force body-level horizontal scroll at 375px — The renderer overrides only h2/h3/pre, so GFM tables and KaTeX display math render bare with no overflow container, and globals.css defines no .katex-display or .prose table overflow rule. The 01-foundations gate table has KaTeX bmatrix matrices in its cells (KaTeX output is white-space:nowrap) and the CNOT truth-table line puts four equations on one nowrap display line - both far exceed the ~343px content box at 375px, so the entire lesson page scrolls horizontally (WCAG 1.4.10 reflow). Unlike code fences, which got conditional focusable scroll regions in the closed 2026-06-17 pass, this overflowing content also has no keyboard-reachable scroll container. _Fix:_ Add a `table` override in makeComponents that wraps the table in a div with overflow-x-auto (reusing CodeBlock's measure-then-expose idiom: tabIndex=0 + role="region" + aria-label only when it actually overflows), and add the KaTeX-documented rule `.katex-display { overflow-x: auto; overflow-y: hidden; }` to globals.css so wide equations scroll inside their own box instead of the page. Impact: High. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/markdown-renderer.tsx:47-89`, `web/src/app/globals.css:3`, `01-foundations/GUIDE.md:158-166`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UX]** Ask-tutor pill and the mobile drawer toggle stack on the same fixed bottom-right slot on every lesson page — In production (NEXT_PUBLIC_TUTOR_URL is set in Amplify), AskTutor renders only on /learn/&lt;slug&gt; routes as a fixed pill at bottom-5 right-5 z-50 with no responsive hiding, while the lesson Sidebar's mobile navigation toggle is fixed at bottom-4 right-4 z-50 (lg:hidden). Their rectangles overlap almost entirely on &lt;lg viewports, and AskTutor is mounted after &lt;main&gt; in the root layout, so at equal z-index the pill paints on top of — and swallows taps meant for — the only mobile navigation affordance on lesson pages. When the drawer is open the pill also floats above the z-40 overlay and covers the drawer's close (X) button. This is invisible in dev, Jest, and Playwright because the tutor env var is absent there, so the pill never renders locally. _Fix:_ Deconflict the two fixed affordances on lesson pages: below lg, offset the AskTutor pill upward (e.g. bottom-20 right-4 so it clears the 48px toggle plus gap) or align both into one shared corner stack with distinct slots; keep desktop placement unchanged. - [x] **[Consistency]** markdown-renderer.test.tsx ships a 60-line fake markdown parser and three tests that only assert the fake's behavior — The oldest of the three renderer suites mocks react-markdown with a hand-written mini parser (headings, code fences, links). Its first three tests ('renders markdown headings', 'renders code blocks', 'renders links') exercise only that mock's regex logic — if react-markdown or the plugin wiring broke, they would stay green. The repo's newer idiom (established in the sibling suites) is the opposite: mock react-markdown as an inert stub and test the REAL code (makeComponents) directly, stating so explicitly. The old suite predates that idiom and now reads as false coverage. _Fix:_ Shrink the mock to a trivial children-passthrough stub (e.g. `({ children }) => <div>{children}</div>`) and delete the three mock-parser tests. Keep the two assertions that test real component behavior: the prose &lt;article&gt; wrapper and the math/content passthrough. Real markdown+KaTeX rendering is already verified end-to-end by the CI build-smoke job the file's own header cites, and fence routing + heading ids are covered by the two sibling suites. Net: ~55 lines of fake parser gone, zero real coverage lost, suite aligned with the repo's stated test idiom. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/__tests__/components/markdown-renderer.test.tsx:15-74`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/__tests__/components/markdown-renderer.test.tsx:82-96`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/__tests__/components/markdown-renderer.fence-routing.test.tsx:9-14`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/__tests__/components/markdown-renderer.headings.test.tsx:10`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Cleaner code]** Renderer hand-rolls hast node types and double-casts around @types/hast, which is guaranteed present as react-markdown's own dependency — markdown-renderer.tsx defines two structural shims (HastTextNode, Positioned), types headingId's node parameter as `unknown` with an internal cast, and uses an `as unknown as HastTextNode` double-cast in pre(). The justifying comment — 'without depending on @types/hast being present' — is stale: react-markdown v10 declares @types/hast ^3.0.0 as a hard dependency (it is installed in web/node_modules/@types/hast), and react-markdown's own Components typing already hands the overrides `node?: Element` in hast terms. The shims re-describe types the compiler already has, and the casts silence checking on the feature's central dispatch path. _Fix:_ Replace the shims with `import type { Element, ElementContent } from "hast"` (types-only, zero runtime): type headingId as (node: Element | undefined), write hastText over ElementContent, and drop both `as unknown as` casts — hast Element's unist position/start/line and Text.value cover everything the code reads. Declare @types/hast explicitly in web/package.json devDependencies so the import doesn't lean on a phantom transitive dependency (flagging per rules: this is a new package.json line, but the package is already on disk and types-only). Future react-markdown node-shape changes then fail at compile time instead of silently returning undefined ids or empty raw text. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/components/markdown-renderer.tsx:22-24`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/components/markdown-renderer.tsx:33-37`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/components/markdown-renderer.tsx:76`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/node_modules/react-markdown/package.json:51`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Disabled 'Run in browser' chip is silent to keyboard, touch, and screen-reader users — Non-runnable notebooks render a span styled like the live Run button with aria-disabled="true" and the explanation only in a title attribute. aria-disabled is not a supported state on the generic span role, so assistive tech ignores it (axe flags aria-allowed-attr): screen-reader users hear plain 'Run in browser' text with no disabled semantics, and because the span is not focusable, keyboard users cannot reach it at all. The reason ('Requires AWS Braket hardware access') lives only in the mouse-hover tooltip, so touch and SR users never learn why the button-looking control does nothing. _Fix:_ Drop the invalid aria-disabled and make the reason real text: append an sr-only qualifier inside the span (e.g. &lt;span className="sr-only"&gt; - unavailable, requires AWS Braket hardware access&lt;/span&gt;) so the chip reads as descriptive text to AT, and consider surfacing the same reason as the visible [11px] caption under the filename on these cards so touch users get it too. No emoji, matches the existing sr-only idiom used elsewhere (sidebar 'completed'). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/notebook-link.tsx:80-86`, `web/src/components/notebook-link.tsx:69-78`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UX]** Fence chrome permanently covers the first code line on touch devices — The code-fence chrome (language chip + wrap toggle + copy) sits absolutely at top-right and is opacity-100 by default, hidden-until-hover only under the can-hover variant. On touch devices it is therefore always visible, and the pre reserves no space for it (px-4 py-3.5), so on a 375px screen the tail of the first one-to-two code lines sits beneath ~120px of opaque bg-gray-800/80 chrome - and horizontally scrolling line 1 to read its end just slides the text under the buttons. Every non-widget fence in every lesson is affected on mobile. _Fix:_ Reserve headroom exactly where the chrome is persistent: `pt-12 can-hover:pt-3.5` on the pre (hover-capable devices keep today's compact padding since their chrome only appears on hover/focus). Static, no measurement needed, and the copy/wrap targets stop competing with content on mobile. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. - [x] **[Security]** Walled lesson content ships in full inside the exported page payloads — auth-wall.tsx documents the sign-up wall as a hard content boundary: 'protected routes pre-render as the gate rather than their content: the content never ships in the static HTML'. That claim is false. AuthWall is a client component, so React Flight serializes its children prop — the entire server-rendered lesson tree from MarkdownRenderer — into every exported /learn page regardless of what the client renders. The current build output confirms it: the visible DOM is only the GateScreen, but the complete lesson (prose, code fences, widget sources) is embedded in the inline RSC payload of the .html and in the adjacent unauthenticated .txt flight segment. View-source or a curl of the .txt recovers the whole walled curriculum. The wall also traded away prerendered first paint (authenticated visitors now get a spinner then a full client-side render of the lesson, including the KaTeX span forests) — and that trade purchased no actual confidentiality. _Fix:_ Refine the claim to match reality: rewrite the auth-wall.tsx comment (and the echo of it in page.tsx:39's noindex comment) to state that the wall hides the rendered DOM and blocks indexing, but the lesson content remains recoverable from the static payloads — it is a sign-up prompt, not a confidentiality boundary. This matters because the pricing/monetization direction leans on the walled platform; decisions should not be built on a documented false belief. Actual content secrecy is impossible under output:"export" from inside the app (Flight must ship the subtree the client may render) — enforcing it would require authenticated delivery of /learn/* at the CDN/Amplify layer, which is infra work explicitly beyond this refine-only pass and should be logged as such. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-wall.tsx:44-48`, `web/src/app/layout.tsx:77`, `web/src/app/learn/[section]/page.tsx:76`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** New robots noindex on lesson pages has no test in the metadata contract suite — Commit a72b705 added robots: { index: false, follow: false } to generateMetadata for every /learn page. This meta tag is the ONLY thing keeping walled lesson URLs out of search indexes: the repo's own sitemap.test.ts documents that robots.txt deliberately allows crawling (a Disallow would cancel the noindex), so the per-page meta is load-bearing with no backstop. Yet learn-section-page.test.tsx — the suite whose stated purpose is the lesson pages' metadata contract (canonical + OG + Twitter, asserted field by field) — never asserts md.robots. A regression that drops or mangles the robots field would pass the entire suite and silently re-expose the gate pages (whose payloads contain the full lesson content) to indexing. _Fix:_ Extend the existing per-section loop in learn-section-page.test.tsx ('keeps a truncation-safe description for every section') with expect(md.robots).toEqual({ index: false, follow: false }) so every curriculum section is covered, and add the inverse assertion where public-route metadata is tested if applicable. One line inside a suite that already iterates getSections(). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/learn/[section]/page.tsx:40`, `web/__tests__/app/learn-section-page.test.tsx:25-68`, `web/__tests__/app/sitemap.test.ts:29-32`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Cleaner code]** Two near-duplicate inline-markdown strippers with divergent regexes live in content.ts and extract-headings.ts — content.ts's stripInlineMarkdown (teasers/meta descriptions) and extract-headings.ts's stripInline (TOC labels + slug source) both unwrap [text](url)/![alt](url) links and emphasis markers, but with subtly different rules: the link regexes differ ([^\]]+ vs [^\]]*, so an empty-label link survives one and not the other), one strips backticks/asterisks wholesale while the other requires balanced pairs, and only one handles __bold__/_italic_. A future markdown-edge fix (e.g. nested emphasis, reference links) applied to one will silently miss the other, letting the meta description and the TOC label for the same GUIDE text diverge. _Fix:_ Extract the shared link-unwrapping + emphasis-stripping core into one helper (a small lib module beside slug.ts) and have each caller apply only its genuinely caller-specific extras (ATX closer trim for headings, underscore emphasis for teasers), so markdown-edge fixes land once. Behavior-pin with the existing content and extract-headings tests before consolidating. Impact: Low. Effort: Medium. - [x] **[Cleaner code]** Widget registry breaks its own uniform pattern for the two no-source widgets, using double-casts and out-of-band entries — 33 of the 35 WIDGETS entries are uniform one-line `lazyWidget(...)` calls, but BlochBuilder and DeviceTable are built differently: two module-level consts force their component types with `as unknown as ComponentType<{ source: string }>` double-casts, and the qbloch/qdevices entries are then hand-assembled objects wrapping them in inline adapters that pass a dummy `source=""`. The registry — the file a maintainer touches every time a widget is added — carries two type lies and two entries that don't look like the others. _Fix:_ Adapt inside the dynamic factory instead of outside it: `qbloch: lazyWidget(() => import("./bloch-builder-widget").then((m) => ({ default: function QBloch() { return <m.BlochBuilder />; } })), tall)` (same for qdevices). A no-props function component is assignable to ComponentType&lt;{source: string}&gt; without any cast, so the two top-level consts, both `as unknown as` casts, the dummy source="" props, and the explanatory comment all disappear, leaving all 35 entries in one uniform shape. Behavior is identical: next/dynamic still provides the same height-matched loading skeleton. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/components/quantum/widget-fence.tsx:58-60`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/components/quantum/widget-fence.tsx:73`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/components/quantum/widget-fence.tsx:77`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Cleaner code]** Lesson page re-inlines the body of buildLineSlugMap instead of sharing the pairing in one helper — extract-headings.ts exports buildLineSlugMap(markdown) whose entire body is `new Map(extractHeadings(markdown).map((h) => [h.line, h.slug]))`. - [x] **[UX]** Sticky 'On this page' rail clips its last entries on short xl viewports — The TOC wrapper is sticky top-24 with no max-height or overflow, and it renders every h2/h3 - 00-prereqs has 18, roughly 630px tall once long labels wrap in the 14rem column. - [x] **[Performance]** KaTeX stylesheet (23.8KB) is bundled globally instead of scoped to math-rendering routes — globals.css line 3 does @import "katex/dist/katex.min.css", so the 23,827-byte KaTeX stylesheet (including 60 @font-face declarations) is compiled into the shared CSS chunk loaded render-blocking on every route — including the public funnel pages (/, /pricing, /login) that render no math at all. The exported shared chunk 0us840gnreyhc.css is 149,745 bytes and contains the katex rules; the landing page links it, so ~16% of the funnel's main stylesheet is dead weight for the exact visitors the conversion surface is built for. Only two components render KaTeX output: the lesson reader's markdown-renderer and the glossary's inline-markdown. _Fix:_ Move the import out of globals.css and into the two consumers: import "katex/dist/katex.min.css" at the top of markdown-renderer.tsx and glossary/inline-markdown.tsx. App Router then attaches it only to route entries that include those components (/learn/*, /glossary/*), trimming ~24KB raw (~6KB gzip) of render-blocking CSS plus 60 font-face parses from every public page, with zero change for lesson pages. Verify with the existing CI build-smoke job that already asserts class="katex" renders in the exported lesson HTML (the import moves later in the cascade than the top-of-globals position; katex- classes are namespaced so collisions are unlikely, but the smoke check confirms it). Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/globals.css:3`, `web/src/components/markdown-renderer.tsx:4,10`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** extractHeadings treats ``` and ~~~ as one interchangeable fence toggle — extract-headings.ts tracks fenced code with a single boolean flipped by FENCE = /^\s*(```|~~~)/ — any line starting with either marker toggles the state. CommonMark (and remark, which the renderer actually uses) closes a fence only with the SAME marker character, so a ~~~ line appearing inside a ``` block (e.g. a lesson explaining Markdown itself, or shell heredoc content) flips inFence off early: subsequent '## ' lines inside the code block become phantom TOC entries whose anchors point at nothing, and real headings after the desync are swallowed (no TOC entry, no id stamped, deep links dead) — all silently, since the renderer's heading ids come from this same map. No GUIDE currently contains ~~~ (verified by grep across 0*-*/GUIDE.md), so this is latent, but GUIDE content is rewritten every content campaign and the failure gives no signal. _Fix:_ Track the opening marker instead of a boolean: on fence open store the matched character (` or ~), and only close when a subsequent fence line uses the same character (matching remark's CommonMark behavior). Add the mixed-marker case to extract-headings.test.ts: a ~~~ line inside a ``` block must not end the fence, and a '## ' line after it must not become a heading. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/extract-headings.ts:22`, `web/src/lib/extract-headings.ts:44-48`, `web/__tests__/lib/extract-headings.test.ts:18-31`, `web/src/components/markdown-renderer.tsx:35-38`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Cleaner code]** ContentData.title and extractTitle are dead — computed for every lesson build, consumed only by a test — getContent() runs extractTitle(markdown) and returns a `title` field, but its single production consumer — the lesson page — destructures only `content.markdown` and `content.notebooks`; the rendered lesson title comes from the GUIDE's own h1 through MarkdownRenderer, and generateMetadata uses section.title from sections.ts instead. The only remaining reference to `.title` anywhere is one assertion in content.test.ts, which pins the dead surface in place and would mislead a future reader into thinking the field is load-bearing. _Fix:_ Delete the `title` field from ContentData, remove extractTitle, and drop the single test assertion (keeping the markdown/notebooks assertions). If a future caller needs the GUIDE h1, extractHeadings/sections.ts already carry the canonical titles. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/content.ts:40,99-102`, `web/src/app/learn/[section]/page.tsx:49,76,86`, `web/__tests__/lib/content.test.ts:8`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)

### 3. In-lesson navigation
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Mobile drawer is `aria-modal` but does not trap focus, inert the background, or lock body scroll — focus moves in and Escape closes (good), but Tab can leave the "modal" into the page behind the overlay, and `aria-modal=true` misreports the background as inert. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:82-90,109-126`) — added 2026-06-17


> **2026-07-19 re-audit** — 18 verified findings. Cross-ref: the shared focus-trap extraction (sidebar is one of the
> three drifted copies) is recorded under ### 1.

- [x] **[Accessibility]** Mobile nav FAB: white icon on accent gradient fails non-text contrast and slips past the contrast guard — The mobile drawer toggle (the only navigation entry point on phones) pairs text-white with a from-accent/to-accent-dark gradient. The repo's own contrast-guard documents white on the solid accent fill as 2.25:1 in light theme, and in the DEFAULT dark theme --accent is oklch(0.85 0.11 118) (bright olive), putting the white hamburger/X glyph around 1.6:1 - far below the 3:1 WCAG 1.4.11 non-text minimum. The guard test never catches it because its regex only matches `bg-accent`, not the gradient utilities `from-accent`/`to-accent`. _Fix:_ Restyle the FAB with the existing `.surface-accent` recipe (neutral high-contrast fill, theme-aware --btn-ink icon), matching the system's own primary-control doctrine - no new tokens needed. Then widen contrast-guard.test.ts's SOLID_ACCENT_FILL regex to also match `from-accent`/`to-accent` gradient utilities so the gradient loophole is closed repo-wide. Impact: High. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:137`, `web/src/app/globals.css:196`, `web/__tests__/contrast-guard.test.ts:20-21`, `web/src/app/globals.css:321-336`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Closed mobile drawer is only translated off-screen - its 7 links stay in the Tab order and accessibility tree — Every auditor examined the drawer's OPEN state (trap, inert, X button, 100vh). Nobody checked the CLOSED state: below lg the aside is hidden purely by `-translate-x-full` - no `visibility: hidden`, no `inert`, no conditional render. A CSS transform does not remove content from the tab order or the accessibility tree, so on every lesson page a mobile keyboard user Tabs through seven invisible links (pressing Enter navigates the page with no visible cause), and mobile screen readers read the entire 'Learning Path' nav plus progress bar as phantom page content while the drawer is visually absent. This violates WCAG 2.4.3 (focus order) and 2.4.7 (focus visible) and is distinct from the auditors' skip-link finding, which is about desktop reading order. _Fix:_ Gate visibility on the open state below lg only: change the conditional to `${open ? "translate-x-0 max-lg:visible" : "-translate-x-full max-lg:invisible"}` and widen the transition to `transition-[transform,visibility]`. CSS visibility is discretely animatable - on close it flips to hidden at the end of the slide-out (animation preserved), on open it flips immediately - and `visibility: hidden` removes the subtree from both the tab order and the accessibility tree while `max-lg:` scoping leaves the always-visible desktop sidebar untouched. Add a Jest regression: with the drawer closed, the aside's className contains `max-lg:invisible`; after toggling, it contains `max-lg:visible`. Impact: High. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:160-162`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:36-59`, `web/__tests__/components/sidebar.test.tsx:44-48`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Architecture]** Drawer's inert-background contract has drifted: Footer and the z-50 AskTutor trigger are never inerted (partial regression of the closed 2026-06-17 modal-a11y item) — The mobile drawer's modal effect marks the background inert by looking up two hardcoded ids, 'site-header' and 'lesson-content'. But the root layout renders two more interactive siblings outside those regions: Footer (about 15 links) and the AskTutor floating trigger. Neither is inerted while the drawer claims aria-modal, so the code's own comment ('making the aria-modal claim truthful') no longer holds. Worse, the AskTutor trigger is fixed at z-50 while the drawer overlay is z-40, so it remains pointer-clickable on top of the scrim while the 'modal' drawer is open. The id-string coupling also fails silently: getElementById returning null is swallowed by optional chaining, so renaming either id would void the protection with no test or runtime signal. _Fix:_ Restore full background coverage and remove the magic-string coupling. Two proven in-repo options: (a) portal the drawer + overlay to document.body (the exact idiom section-gate-modal.tsx already uses via createPortal) and inert every other body child while open, which stays correct as the layout grows; or (b) minimally, export shared id constants from one module, add the footer and tutor-trigger regions to the inert set, and ensure the overlay stacks above every non-drawer z-50 element. Either way, add a test asserting the footer/tutor trigger are inert while the drawer is open so future layout additions cannot silently re-drift. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:89-92`, `web/src/app/layout.tsx:79-80`, `web/src/components/ask-tutor.tsx:189`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:147`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UX]** TOC 'lockstep' highlight goes blank for most of the read inside any section longer than ~30% of the viewport — useActiveHeading only marks a heading active while its element intersects the top-30% viewport band (rootMargin '0px 0px -70% 0px'). Once a section's heading scrolls above the viewport top and before the next heading reaches the 30% line, the visible set is empty and active is set to null - so while reading the body of any section taller than ~30% of the viewport (nearly every GUIDE section; they carry 13-18 headings across long prose), the rail shows NO current position. The feature's promise is a TOC 'kept in lockstep', but the highlight is off more often than on. _Fix:_ Refine the hook to keep the last heading that scrolled past the trigger line active: on each observer callback, for entries leaving upward (boundingClientRect.top &lt; 0) record them as 'passed', and pick the topmost visible heading OR, when none is visible, the last passed one; return null only when nothing has been passed (the intro case the comment already wants). Update the test at table-of-contents.test.tsx:103 to assert the retained-highlight contract instead. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/table-of-contents.tsx:27`, `web/src/components/table-of-contents.tsx:29`, `web/__tests__/components/table-of-contents.test.tsx:103-123`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Performance]** View-transition callback never awaits route commit, so slow navigations get a no-op fade plus hard cut — TransitionLink's update callback calls router.push() and returns undefined, so the browser captures the 'new' snapshot as soon as the callback's microtask settles. router.push commits asynchronously (React transition lane, and a network fetch on prefetch-cache miss), so on any navigation that is not already in the prefetch cache the transition animates old-frame to identical old-frame, and the real content swap lands afterward as exactly the hard cut the component exists to prevent. Prefetched sidebar links usually commit fast enough to win the race, which is why it looks fine in the common case — the animation silently degrades precisely on the slow navigations where perceived smoothness matters most. _Fix:_ Have the update callback return a promise that resolves when the navigation commits: module-scoped `let resolveNav: (() => void) | null`, callback does `router.push(...); return new Promise<void>((r) => { resolveNav = r; })`, and a small `useEffect` on `usePathname()` inside TransitionLink calls `resolveNav?.()` on change, with a ~1s `setTimeout` fallback so an aborted navigation cannot stall the capture (the browser hard-caps a pending VT at 4s of frozen rendering). Extend transition-link.test.tsx to assert the callback's promise resolves on pathname change and on timeout. No new dependencies; pure refinement of the existing animation path. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/transition-link.tsx:43`, `web/src/app/globals.css:621-628`, `web/src/components/transition-link.tsx:39-40`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UI]** Sidebar and TOC never finished the PR #169 token migration - cool grays, pure white, and a stale pre-redesign teal glow — PR #169 moved the shell onto warm glass tokens (hue-88 surfaces, --bd/--track/--field, olive accent 118), but the sidebar and TOC still mix in pre-redesign values: cool Tailwind grays for hovers/chips/track/rail text, a pure-white light-theme drawer over the warm paper base, and - most visibly - the overall-progress bar's glow hardcodes oklch hue 192 (the OLD teal accent, now only section 0's identity hue) under a bar that is an olive 118 gradient, producing a cyan halo around an olive fill in both themes. _Fix:_ Sweep both components onto the existing tokens: `var(--bar-glow)` for the progress glow (kills the teal remnant and makes it theme-aware), `bg-(--track)` for the progress track, `bg-(--surface-1)`-based mix (mirroring the dark side's color-mix) for the light drawer, `bg-(--field)`/`hover:bg-(--field)` for chip and hover fills, and `border-(--bd)` + `text-(--mut)` on the TOC rail. Zero new CSS - every replacement token already exists and is used by the header ten lines away. _Subsumes the narrower sidebar progress-glow reports from the F2 and F5 audits._ Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:190-191`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:184`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:160`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:43,52`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Drawer focus trap excludes the visible X close button - Tab can never reach it while the drawer is open — When the mobile drawer opens, the trap collects focusables only from inside the aside, but the toggle button (which now renders as the X close affordance, floating above the overlay at z-50) is a sibling outside the aside. Keyboard users see an X they can never Tab to; the only keyboard exits are Escape (undiscoverable) since overlay click is pointer-only. The APG modal pattern expects the dialog's visible close control inside the Tab cycle. _Fix:_ Include the toggle in the cycle: build the focusables list as `[toggleRef.current, ...aside.querySelectorAll(...)]` (or treat the toggle as the wrap point) so Tab order runs X button -&gt; drawer links -&gt; back to X. Because the aside is position:fixed, its DOM position is layout-free: it can sit after the content with zero visual change. _Fix:_ In page.tsx, render &lt;Sidebar /&gt; after the #lesson-content div (and after the TOC aside). - [x] **[UI]** Drawer height uses 100vh, clipping the last section links behind iOS Safari's expanded toolbar — The drawer is sized h-[calc(100vh-4rem)]. - [x] **[Cleaner code]** TransitionLink advertises LinkProps['href'] (string | UrlObject) but navigates via String(href) — The component's prop type accepts Next's full Url type, yet the click handler calls router.push(String(href)). Passing a UrlObject - which the declared type invites - would stringify to '[object Object]' and navigate to garbage, but only on primary clicks with the View Transitions path active (modified clicks and reduced-motion fall through to &lt;Link&gt;, which handles objects fine), making it an inconsistent, hard-to-diagnose latent bug. Every current call site (sidebar, prev-next, section-card, section-gate-modal, glossary components) passes a template string, so the wide type buys nothing. _Fix:_ Make the contract honest: narrow the prop to href: string (Omit 'href' from LinkProps and redeclare), so a future UrlObject caller gets a compile error instead of a broken navigation, and the String() coercion becomes a plain pass-through. - [x] **[Resilience & tests]** PrevNext with an unrecognized slug renders a misleading 'Next' link to the first section, and the test enshrines it — When currentSlug matches no section, findIndex returns -1, so prev = sections[-2] = undefined but next = sections[0] — the component renders a 'Next: Prerequisites' card that is navigationally wrong (the reader is not before section 00). Today's only caller validates the slug via notFound() first, but the unit test explicitly locks in the accidental behavior instead of guarding an intended one, so any future caller (review dashboard, playground handoff) passing a stale slug inherits a confidently wrong nav card that a green suite endorses. _Fix:_ Add an early guard in PrevNext — `if (currentIndex === -1) return null;` — and flip the prev-next.test.tsx case to assert that an unrecognized slug renders no links. - [x] **[UX]** Cmd/ctrl-click on a drawer link (open lesson in new tab) still slides the drawer shut with no focus return — TransitionLink invokes the consumer's onClick before its own modified-click guard, and SidebarItem's onNavigate is an unconditional `setOpen(false)` - not `close()`. So a cmd/ctrl/shift-click that opens the lesson in a background tab (a flow TransitionLink's guard explicitly preserves) also closes the drawer in the current tab even though no navigation happened there, and because `close()` is bypassed, focus is never returned to the toggle - it stays stranded on the link that just translated off-screen. The auditors reviewed TransitionLink's guard and the drawer's trap separately; the seam between them is where this lives. _Fix:_ Have the drawer ignore modified/aux clicks when deciding to close: pass the event through (`onNavigate={(e) => { if (e.defaultPrevented || e.metaKey || e.ctrlKey || e.shiftKey || e.altKey || e.button !== 0) return; setOpen(false); }}`). Export that predicate (e.g. `isModifiedClick(e)`) from transition-link.tsx and reuse it in both files so the two guards cannot drift - which also feeds the auditors' extract-shared-logic theme without adding any capability. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/transition-link.tsx:26-37`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:203`, `web/src/components/sidebar.tsx:75-78`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** Vestigial next/link mocks in sidebar and prev-next test suites never engage - dead scaffolding from before TransitionLink — Both suites mock next/link AND @/components/transition-link, but Sidebar and PrevNext render exclusively through TransitionLink (which the second mock replaces with a plain anchor), so the next/link mock is unreachable dead code left behind when these components migrated to TransitionLink. It misleads the next maintainer into believing the components still consume next/link directly, and it quietly masks any future regression where someone reintroduces a raw Link (the test would keep passing identically instead of surfacing the inconsistency). _Fix:_ Delete the `jest.mock("next/link", ...)` blocks from sidebar.test.tsx and prev-next.test.tsx, keeping only the TransitionLink mock each suite actually exercises. Pure removal - if either suite then fails, that failure is itself the signal that a raw next/link crept back into these components. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. ### 4. Dark / light theme
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Theme toggle never announces state and keys off `theme` not `resolvedTheme` — `aria-label` is a static "Toggle theme" (icon is `aria-hidden`), and with `enableSystem` set a `"system"` value would mismatch the shown icon and first-click target. Derive icon + dynamic label ("Switch to light/dark theme") from `resolvedTheme`. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/theme-toggle.tsx:9,16,18-28`, `web/src/app/layout.tsx:28`) — added 2026-06-17


> **2026-07-19 re-audit** — 18 verified findings on the fresh #169 Instrument token system. Cross-ref: the FogField
> per-frame render loop is recorded under ### 1.

- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** All WCAG claims of the fresh #169 token system are comment-only; both contrast tests are class-string greps blind to token values - and one claim is already false — PR #169 moved contrast-critical colors into runtime oklch custom properties (--mut, --btn-fill/--btn-ink, --accent per theme, chip-selected fill), but the two guard suites only grep Tailwind class strings: contrast-guard checks for the `bg-accent`+`text-white` pairing and caption-contrast checks only that `.text-caption` contains `var(--mut)`. Nothing computes contrast from the actual token values, so retuning any oklch value in globals.css can silently break AA in one theme. This is not hypothetical: the light-theme `--accent` is commented "legible on light bg" but computes to 2.79:1 against --surface-base (fails 4.5:1 AA and even 3:1 large-text), and it is used as resting text via `text-accent` on eyebrow micro-labels; meanwhile the --mut comment claims ~4.9:1 on light where the real value is 6.54:1 - documented numbers drift with nothing failing. _Fix:_ Add one unit suite (e.g. web/__tests__/token-contrast.test.ts) with ~30 lines of dependency-free oklch-&gt;linear-sRGB-&gt;WCAG-luminance math that parses the light and dark token blocks out of globals.css and asserts minimum ratios for each pairing the comments promise: --ink and --mut on --surface-base/-1/-2, --btn-ink on --btn-fill, gray-950 on --accent (.chip-selected), and --accent/--accent-dark wherever used as resting text - in BOTH themes. This pins every future token retune to a computed number instead of a comment, and immediately surfaces the existing light-theme text-accent failure for a deliberate decision (e.g. mapping light-theme micro-label text to --accent-dark, which computes 4.93:1). Impact: High. Effort: Medium. (`web/__tests__/contrast-guard.test.ts:20-21`, `web/__tests__/caption-contrast.test.ts:72`, `web/src/app/globals.css:156`, `web/src/app/page.tsx:240`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** Focus indicator fails 3:1 non-text contrast in the light theme (1.60:1) — The site-wide .focus-ring utility draws a 2px ring in accent at 50% alpha. The light theme's --accent is oklch(0.66 0.1 118); composited at 50% over the light --surface-base it renders #c1c8a1, which measures 1.60:1 against the surface — far below the 3:1 WCAG 1.4.11 requirement for focus indicators (even at full alpha the light accent only reaches 2.79:1). The dark theme passes (3.81:1 blended). Keyboard users in light mode get a barely-visible focus ring on every interactive element: nav links, the theme toggle, the skip link, all CTAs. _Fix:_ Make the ring color a per-theme token like every other Instrument color: add e.g. --focus: var(--accent-dark) (oklch(0.52 0.1 118), ~5:1 solid on the light surface) under :root and --focus: var(--accent) under .dark in the existing @layer base blocks, then change .focus-ring to `focus-visible:ring-(--focus)` and drop the /50 alpha (keep it only on dark if the softer look is wanted there, where it still clears 3:1). One utility edit fixes focus visibility everywhere at once. Impact: High. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/globals.css:454-456`, `web/src/app/globals.css:156`, `web/src/components/theme-toggle.tsx:21`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Architecture]** bg-atmosphere/-light and bg-grid-dots/-light are the only theme-paired class duos in a var-driven token system — Every other theme-dependent value in the Instrument system flips through one runtime var set under :root/.dark (--glass, --bd, --ink, --bar-fill, --shadow-*, --accent...). The atmosphere and grid-dot backgrounds instead exist as light/dark class pairs, forcing every consumer to write the double-class incantation 'bg-atmosphere-light dark:bg-atmosphere' - currently repeated at 8+ page shells - and making a silent wrong-theme background possible if a callsite drops the dark: prefix or pairs them backwards. The reduced-motion drift gate must also enumerate both classes (:552-557) instead of one. _Fix:_ Hoist the two radial-gradient stacks into an --atmosphere var (and the dot color into --grid-dot) set in the existing :root and .dark blocks, make .bg-atmosphere and .bg-grid-dots read the vars, delete the -light variants, and collapse each callsite to the single class. One utility per surface, theme resolution in the same place as every other token, no possible mispairing, and the motion gate names one class. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/app/globals.css:538`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/app/page.tsx:222`, `/Users/cperez/dev/altivum-dev/quantum/web/src/app/globals.css:552`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Consistency]** Two parallel ink systems ship: 23 headings still wear text-gray-900 dark:text-white beside 112 text-(--ink) — cool pure-white vs the warm Instrument ink — The #169 token system routes body/heading ink through the warm runtime vars --ink and --mut, but a fifth of the app's heading tier and 33 muted-text sites still use the legacy cool-gray Tailwind pairs. These are not the same color: gray-900 is Tailwind's cool blue-gray and dark:text-white is pure #fff, versus the warm hue-82 --ink values — so identical heading tiers visibly shift in temperature between pages (e.g. /pricing warm vs /glossary and /learn cool), and some single elements mix both systems. The auditors flagged only the theme toggle's hover fill; the same drift runs through the text-color tier app-wide. _Fix:_ Mechanically converge the remaining legacy pairs onto the tokens they duplicate: text-gray-900 dark:text-white → text-(--ink); text-gray-600/700 dark pairs → text-(--mut) (or .text-caption where it is caption-tier); border-gray-200 dark:border-white/10 → border-(--bd). Roughly 56 call sites, all one-class swaps; afterwards the ink tier has a single source of truth and heading temperature stops shifting between routes. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. - [x] **[Resilience & tests]** Reduced-motion fallback clamps animation-duration but not iteration-count, so escaped infinite animations flicker for exactly the users who opted out of motion — The global reduce block sets `animation-duration: 0.01ms !important` but omits the canonical companion `animation-iteration-count: 1 !important`. Any infinite animation not individually opted out therefore keeps cycling: a 0.01ms infinite animation samples an essentially arbitrary progress on every frame, turning a spinner into frame-random rotation jitter and a skeleton pulse into opacity flicker, while keeping an active animation ticking style recalc forever. Two live consumers escape the per-utility opt-outs today: the AuthWall verifying spinner and the QPU panel skeleton both use Tailwind's infinite `animate-spin`/`animate-pulse` with no `motion-reduce:animate-none`. _Fix:_ Add `animation-iteration-count: 1 !important;` to the existing reduce block (one line), making the global fallback actually freeze any infinite animation that forgets the per-element `motion-reduce:animate-none`; also add the missing `motion-reduce:animate-none` to the two escapees to match the repo idiom used everywhere else. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. - [x] **[Cleaner code]** .glass opaque fallback is dead code - the documented --surface-1 fallback can never engage — The .glass recipe stacks two background-color declarations intending a fallback: 'Falls back to the opaque --surface-1 where backdrop-filter is unsupported' (comment at globals.css:300-303). But the double-declaration fallback trick only works when the second value fails to parse; here both values are always-valid var() references defined in :root/.dark, so the second (var(--glass), a 4.5%-alpha white in dark / 60%-alpha white in light) unconditionally wins in every browser. In a browser without backdrop-filter (the @supports block only adds the blur, it does not gate the translucent fill), .glass renders as a nearly transparent fill with no blur - not the documented opaque surface. The first declaration is dead in all browsers and the comment misdocuments the actual behavior on the flagship surface recipe of the fresh #169 system. _Fix:_ Move the background-color: var(--glass) declaration (and the glass-2 variant if desired) inside the existing @supports (backdrop-filter...) block, leaving background-color: var(--surface-1) as the base declaration. The documented fallback becomes real, the dead declaration disappears, and the comment becomes true - no visual change in any backdrop-filter-capable browser. Impact: Low. Effort: Low.
