- [x] **[Performance]** body gradient uses background-attachment: fixed, which de-optimizes scrolling in engines that repaint fixed-attachment backgrounds — The base smoke gradient is attached to body with `background-attachment: fixed`. Desktop Safari and some Chromium paths cannot composite fixed-attachment backgrounds and fall back to repainting the background on scroll, and iOS Safari has historically mis-handled fixed attachment on body outright. On long lesson pages this adds scroll-time paint work underneath the already-costly .glass backdrop-filter surfaces - while the same viewport-pinned look is available for free from a composited fixed layer, which the design already uses for the fog canvas one z-level up. _Fix:_ Move the gradient off background-attachment: fixed onto a guaranteed-composited fixed layer: either a `body::before { position: fixed; inset: 0; z-index: -20; background: linear-gradient(...); }` or the existing FogField wrapper. Identical visual (gradient pinned to viewport), but scrolling never repaints it in any engine. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/globals.css:229-233`, `web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:152`, `web/src/app/globals.css:310-315`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** FogField samples prefers-reduced-motion once at mount and never listens for changes — the only animation in the system that ignores a live OS toggle — Every CSS animation in the design system responds instantly when the user flips the OS reduce-motion setting, because media queries re-evaluate live. FogField instead freezes the preference into a const at mount: a user who enables reduce-motion mid-session keeps the full-viewport infinite rAF loop running until a reload, and one who disables it is stuck with a frozen frame. This is orthogonal to the auditors' 60fps-cost finding — their pause-when-hidden fix would not make the field honor a live preference change. _Fix:_ Hold the MediaQueryList from the existing matchMedia call, subscribe to its 'change' event in the same effect, and on change update the flag, cancel or restart the rAF loop, and repaint one static frame — exactly mirroring the reseed path the component already runs for theme flips at lines 130-138. Cleanup alongside the existing listeners. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/fog-field.tsx:26`, `fog-field.tsx:119-138`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Cleaner code]** focus-ring's dark: ring-offset variant re-applies the identical --surface-base var — a no-op duplicate in the app's most-used utility — The .focus-ring recipe sets the ring offset color to the runtime var --surface-base and then sets the exact same var again under the dark: variant. Because --surface-base already flips with the theme in @layer base, the dark: clause is dead weight that generates a redundant compiled rule and misleads readers into thinking the offset differs per theme — the same pre-runtime-var reflex the auditors caught elsewhere, surviving inside the token file itself. _Fix:_ Delete the 'dark:focus-visible:ring-offset-(--surface-base)' clause from .focus-ring. Identical rendered output in both themes, one fewer compiled dark-variant rule, and the utility reads as the runtime-var pattern it actually is. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/globals.css:455`, `globals.css:160`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)

### 5. Progress tracking
- [x] **[Performance]** Unscoped cross-tab `storage` listener recomputes on every unrelated localStorage write — `subscribe` passes the callback straight to `addEventListener("storage", ...)`, so theme/review/pyodide-cache writes in another tab all re-run `completedCount`/`isSectionComplete`. Filter on `e.key` (`null` or starts with `qc:`). Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/progress-store.ts:53-61`) — added 2026-06-17


> **2026-07-19 re-audit** — 11 verified findings. Cross-ref: the sidebar progress-bar teal glow is inside ### 3's
> token-migration entry.

- [x] **[Consistency]** The "qc-progress" event name is hardcoded at four dispatch/listen sites despite PROGRESS_EVENT_NAME existing to single-source it — The event channel IS the progress feature's cross-module contract (store writes, Rep widgets, sync debounce, and every useSyncExternalStore subscriber all meet on this one string), and progress-store.ts exports PROGRESS_EVENT_NAME precisely to single-source it. Four modules follow that pattern, but four other sites re-type the raw literal "qc-progress". A future typo at any raw-literal dispatch site fails silently: the write lands in localStorage but the sidebar/catalog never refresh and the sync debounce never arms — no error, just stale UI and unsynced progress. The literal inside progress-merge.ts also reveals a boundary wrinkle: it cannot import the constant because progress-store.ts:10 already imports registerLocalDeletion/clearLocalDeletion FROM progress-merge (a cycle), so the contract's name currently cannot live where its writers need it. _Fix:_ Hoist the constant to a leaf so every writer and listener can import it: declare `export const PROGRESS_EVENT_NAME = "qc-progress"` in a dependency-free spot (a two-line progress-event.ts, or the top of progress-merge.ts which imports only review-schedule), re-export it from progress-store.ts so all eight existing importers keep their import path unchanged, and replace the raw literals at progress-merge.ts:256, sync-client.ts:231, delete-account.tsx:58, and progress-sync.tsx:99/105 with the constant. This also collapses the PROGRESS_EVENT / PROGRESS_EVENT_NAME dual naming inside progress-store.ts. No behavior change; the existing dispatch-count tests (circuit-store.test.ts, progress-merge.test.ts) keep guarding the contract. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/progress-store.ts:13`, `web/src/lib/progress-store.ts:10`, `web/src/lib/progress-merge.ts:256`, `web/src/lib/sync-client.ts:231`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** Second same-device tab defeats the un-complete tombstone: sync re-adopts the server copy under the learner's click — The documented invariant that un-completing a section 'does not silently re-adopt the server's copy under the learner's click' only holds in the tab where the click happened. The tombstone registry is per-tab module state, but localStorage is shared across tabs. Un-complete in tab A removes the shared qc:section key and tombstones it only in tab A's Set; tab B (signed-in, sync configured) runs its own arrival/debounced sync, exports a snapshot without the key, merges the server's '1' back in one-sided, and applySnapshot in tab B - which has no tombstone - writes '1' straight back into the SHARED localStorage. Tab A's own storage listener then re-renders the section as Completed, silently reverting the learner's explicit undo. _Fix:_ Extend the existing session-tombstone semantics to all tabs of the device (still session-scoped, still never propagating deletion cross-device): install one 'storage' listener - e.g. where the sync driver mounts, or exported from progress-merge.ts - that on e.key?.startsWith('qc:') calls registerLocalDeletion(e.key) when e.newValue === null and clearLocalDeletion(e.key) when it is non-null. This mirrors the exact removeItem/setItem calls writeFlag already makes, so tab B refuses to re-adopt precisely the keys tab A deleted, and re-completing anywhere clears the tombstone everywhere. Add a jsdom test that dispatches StorageEvent({key:'qc:section:x', newValue:null}) and asserts applySnapshot({'qc:section:x':'1'}) leaves localStorage empty. No new capability - it closes the gap in an already-documented guarantee. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. - [x] **[Consistency]** usePersistentSolved hand-rolls a private subscriber that drops the cross-tab storage leg progress-store.subscribe already provides — progress-store's header sells 'one channel' where a solved challenge and a completed section notify any subscriber through one listener, and its exported subscribe() implements that channel as TWO legs: the in-tab qc-progress event plus the qc:*-filtered cross-tab 'storage' event. But use-persistent-solved.ts — the shared solved-flag hook for all six Rep widgets — bypasses subscribe() and inlines its own subscriber with only the in-tab leg. - [x] **[Architecture]** Two near-identical scan-and-wipe loops over the qc:* progress contract can drift independently — The "remove every qc:* key, then notify progress subscribers" dance is implemented twice: delete-account.tsx's clearLocal and sync-client.ts's resetLocalProgress. Both iterate localStorage by index, collect keys with the qc: prefix, remove them, and dispatch the progress event — but they already differ in two quiet ways (clearLocal additionally sweeps the qc-sync:meta key and dispatches unconditionally; resetLocalProgress guards the dispatch on keys.length &gt; 0). One of those differences is intentional (meta handling), the other is accidental drift. Because the wipe defines what "all progress" means to the sync contract, a future key-family addition or dispatch fix applied to one loop and not the other produces surfaces that disagree about what a wipe covers. _Fix:_ Extract one helper next to the contract's other storage-scan code (progress-merge.ts, or the same leaf module as the event constant from the other finding): e.g. `wipeLocalProgress(alsoKeys?: string[]): number` that scans, removes qc:* plus any explicitly passed keys, and fires the progress event once when anything was removed. resetLocalProgress becomes a one-line call; clearLocal calls it with ["qc-sync:meta"]. The intentional meta difference becomes an explicit argument instead of a divergence a reader must diff two files to discover, and the dispatch-guard inconsistency disappears. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/delete-account.tsx:50-62`, `web/src/lib/sync-client.ts:223-233`, `web/src/lib/progress-merge.ts:71-84`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Accessibility]** SectionProgress toggle changes its accessible name and aria-pressed at once, against APG and the repo's own toggle idiom — The "Mark as complete" button encodes completion state in two channels simultaneously: aria-pressed flips true AND the accessible name flips to "Completed". The ARIA APG button pattern explicitly warns not to change a toggle's label while aria-pressed is used. In practice, on activation AT announces only the pressed-state change while the name silently flips, and on later encounters the button reads double-encoded ("Completed, pressed, toggle button"). The repo elsewhere follows the conforming pattern — code-block's wrap toggle keeps a constant aria-label with aria-pressed carrying state — so this button is also internally inconsistent with house idiom. _Fix:_ Pick one state channel. Since the visible label flip ("Completed") is a deliberate design and WCAG 2.5.3 Label-in-Name forbids masking it with a divergent constant aria-label, the cleanest fix is to drop aria-pressed and let the flipping name be the single source of state (re-announced on focus/browse), mirroring the sidebar's plain sr-only "completed" wording at sidebar.tsx:58. Alternatively keep aria-pressed and hold the name constant — but do not ship both changing together. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/section-progress.tsx:34`, `web/src/components/section-progress.tsx:50`, `web/src/components/code-block.tsx:64-66`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[UX]** With storage blocked, "Mark as complete" is a dead control with zero feedback — When localStorage access throws (Chrome/Safari with "block all cookies" / site data blocked), writeFlag's catch swallows the write AND the qc-progress dispatch, and readFlag returns false — so clicking "Mark as complete" changes nothing: no button flip, no sidebar checkmark, no error, and clicking again does the same. The module's own header promises graceful degradation ("progress just isn't remembered this session"), but the actual behavior is a fully inert control, which reads as the site being broken rather than storage being off. _Fix:_ Make the code match its documented degradation: add a module-level in-memory Map&lt;string, boolean&gt; fallback in progress-store — writeFlag records into it when setItem throws and still dispatches PROGRESS_EVENT; readFlag consults it when getItem throws. The toggle, sidebar checkmarks, and completion count then work for the session (merely not persisted), with no new UI and every consumer (isSectionComplete, completedCount, workspace.ts) picking it up through the existing read path. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/progress-store.ts:25-41`, `web/src/lib/progress-store.ts:17-23`, `web/src/components/section-progress.tsx:31-50`) — added 2026-07-19 — DONE 2026-07-19 (PR #172)
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** Delete-account's clearLocal leaves stale un-complete tombstones armed while also removing the account fence that would reset them — Session tombstones (registered when a learner un-completes a section) live in module state and are only ever reset inside runSync's boundSub-mismatch branch. DeleteAccount.clearLocal wipes every qc:* key AND qc-sync:meta but never calls resetLocalDeletions() — and wiping the meta erases boundSub, so the mismatch branch (the one place the reset lives) can no longer trigger. Un-complete section X, delete account A, then sign in as existing account B via email/password in the same tab (no reload, so module state survives): B's first sync adopts as a first-ever sync, and applySnapshot silently skips B's qc:section:X='1' under A's stale tombstone — B's completed section is missing on this device until a reload. _Fix:_ Call resetLocalDeletions() inside clearLocal (exported from progress-merge, already in the dependency graph): once this device's local copy is wiped, records of what this device deleted are wiped with it, so the next account's first sync applies its full server snapshot. One line plus a unit test in delete-account.test.tsx asserting a registered tombstone no longer suppresses a post-deletion applySnapshot. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. ### 6. Foundations explorables

> **Clean verification pass — 2026-06-20.** The adversarial verify stage that was server-throttled on the 2026-06-17 run completed cleanly here (19 findings survived independent skeptic review). _Current state:_ The core quantum math is sound — Bloch vectors and probability bars are correct across all widgets — and the two genuine correctness items found this pass are cosmetic edge cases (a gate-chip label/convention mismatch that only surfaces when cross-referencing the copied amplitudes, and a ~1-in-2^53 zero-probability sampler draw). The largest opportunities are an always-on 3D render loop and substantial DRY cleanup across the circuit-family widgets (gate chips, state readout, probability bars), plus several screen-reader and touch-target accessibility refinements.

- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-20 (WS-1) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **3D Bloch &lt;Canvas&gt; runs a 60fps render loop forever (frameloop defaults to 'always')**. BlochSphere3D mounts a react-three-fiber &lt;Canvas&gt; with no frameloop prop, so it defaults to 'always' and re-renders the WebGL scene 60 times a second for the entire life of the component — even after the StateVector lerp has converged on its target and the user is not dragging OrbitControls. Every Foundations widget that shows the 3D sphere (BlochBuilder, WavefunctionScrubber, ScrollySection) keeps a GPU/CPU loop spinning indefinitely while the visual is completely static, and a lesson page can have several such canvases at once, each with its own independent always-on loop. _Fix:_ In bloch-sphere-3d.tsx, set `frameloop="demand"` on the &lt;Canvas&gt;, and in StateVector pull `invalidate` from `useThree()` and call it from useFrame only while the vector is still moving (e.g. while `current.current.distanceToSquared(target) &gt; epsilon`); also drive renders on interaction by passing `onChange={() =&gt; invalidate()}` (or relying on drei OrbitControls' demand integration). This stops the loop within a few frames of the lerp settling and resumes it on drag or a new target. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (bloch-sphere-3d.tsx:148 - `&lt;Canvas camera={{ position: [1.6, 1.2, 2.2], fov: 45 }} dpr={[1, 2]}&gt;` sets no `frameloop`, so R3F v9 (@react-three/fiber ^9.6.1) uses the default `'always'` continuous render loop · bloch-sphere-3d.tsx:49-58 - `useFrame(() =&gt; { current.current.lerp(target, 0.18); ... })` runs every frame unconditionally with no convergence check; once `current ≈ target` it keeps lerping by a negligible delta forever, so the loop never has a reason to stop on its own · grep across web/src/components/quantum confirms zero `frameloop`/`invalidate` usages anywhere) — added 2026-06-20

- [x] **[Correctness]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-2b) — ✓verified — NEW — **BlochBuilder's 'RY θ RZ φ' gate-chip mislabels a state computed with a different phase convention**. The widget shows a gate-sequence chip reading 'RY θ RZ φ' (implying the state is RZ(φ)·RY(θ)|0&gt;), but the Dirac string and copy-as-Python output are computed by stateFromAngles, which uses the convention cos(θ/2)|0&gt; + e^{iφ}sin(θ/2)|1&gt; (the entire relative phase placed on |1&gt;). RZ(φ)·RY(θ)|0&gt; actually equals e^{-iφ/2}cos(θ/2)|0&gt; + e^{+iφ/2}sin(θ/2)|1&gt;, which differs by a non-trivial per-amplitude phase split. A learner who runs the labeled gate sequence in the WavefunctionScrubber (qsim 'RY 0 θ / RZ 0 φ') or pastes the labeled gates into Python gets a different amplitude string than the widget's own readout — e.g. for θ=π/2, φ=π/2 the widget prints 0.71|0&gt; + 0.71i|1&gt; while the labeled gates give (0.5-0.5i)|0&gt; + (0.5+0.5i)|1&gt;. _Fix:_ In bloch-builder.ts, make stateFromAngles actually apply RZ(φ)·RY(θ)|0&gt; (reuse scrolly.ts stateForAngles / math.ts ry+rz so all foundations explorables share one convention), OR change the chip label in bloch-builder-widget.tsx:33 to reflect the canonical-phase convention it currently uses (e.g. drop the gate-sequence framing and label it |ψ⟩ = cos(θ/2)|0&gt; + e^{iφ}sin(θ/2)|1&gt;). The Bloch vector is identical either way, so only the displayed/copied amplitudes change; aligning with scrolly.ts's real-gate convention also makes the qbloch and qscrub widgets agree. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (bloch-builder-widget.tsx:33 - const gateSeq = `RY ${theta.toFixed(2)}  RZ ${phi.toFixed(2)}`; advertises the state as RZ(φ)RY(θ)|0&gt; · bloch-builder.ts:4-11 - stateFromAngles returns [c,0] and [s*cos(phi), s*sin(phi)], i.e. cos(θ/2)|0&gt; + e^{iφ}sin(θ/2)|1&gt;, phase entirely on |1&gt; (no e^{-iφ/2} on |0&gt;) · math.ts:54-58 - rz(theta) = diag(c-si, c+si) = diag(e^{-iφ/2}, e^{+iφ/2}); applied as RZ(φ)RY(θ)|0&gt; this splits the phase across both amplitudes, not matching stateFromAngles · bloch-builder-widget.tsx:78-83 - the Dirac string and Copy-as-Python button both serialize this non-RZ·RY state, so the copied artifact disagrees with the displayed gate sequence and with the scrubber running the same labeled gates) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Correctness]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-2b) — ✓verified — NEW — **Inverse-transform samplers can emit a zero-probability basis state when rng() returns exactly 0**. Both Born-rule samplers select an outcome with the predicate `r &lt;= acc` where r = rng()*total. Math.random() can legitimately return exactly 0, giving r=0, which satisfies `0 &lt;= cdf[0]` and returns index 0 even when probs[0] === 0. For a circuit whose first basis state has zero amplitude (e.g. an entangled state with probabilities [0, 0.5, 0.5, 0], or a product state with no |00&gt; component), this yields a physically impossible measurement outcome — the CorrelationDemo can tally a |00&gt; count for a Bell-like state that should never produce it, and the ShotsSampler can place a shot on a zero-probability bar. _Fix:_ In shots.ts and correlation.ts, skip zero-probability buckets — either advance past any leading prob===0 entries before returning, or change the cumulative comparison so an outcome with zero mass is never selected (e.g. accumulate and return the first index where acc &gt; r with a strict comparison, falling back to the last non-zero bucket). A single shared sampler used by both call sites would fix it in one place. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (correlation.ts:25-30 - sampleOutcome: `const r = rng()*total; ... if (r &lt;= acc) return i;` returns i=0 whenever r=0 regardless of whether probs[0] is 0 · shots.ts:11-17 - sampleCounts binary search with `if (r &lt;= cdf[mid]) hi = mid` collapses to lo=0 when r=0, even if cdf[0]===0 (probs[0]===0) · correlation-demo.tsx:132-137 - handleMeasure feeds these indices straight into the visible tally, so a zero-probability |00&gt;/|11&gt; can be displayed for the entangled panel) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-20 (WS-1) — ✓verified — NEW — **Three great-circle point arrays are rebuilt on every state change in Scene**. Scene calls circlePoints('equator'/'xz'/'yz') directly in JSX with no memoization, each building a fresh 65-element array of 3-tuples. Scene re-renders whenever the `state` prop changes — which happens on every slider drag tick in BlochBuilder and every scrub step / scroll rAF in WavefunctionScrubber and ScrollySection — so these three static ring geometries are reallocated and the drei &lt;Line&gt; meshes regenerate their geometry on input that never actually moves them. _Fix:_ In bloch-sphere-3d.tsx, hoist the three circlePoints(...) results and the static axis-line point literals to module-level constants (they never depend on state), or wrap them in useMemo with an empty dep list inside Scene. The rings and axes are fixed geometry; only StateVector should react to `state`. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (bloch-sphere-3d.tsx:102-104 - `&lt;Line points={circlePoints("equator")} ... /&gt;`, `circlePoints("xz")`, `circlePoints("yz")` are invoked inline on each Scene render; circlePoints (lines 29-40) loops 65 times allocating `[number,number,number]` tuples each call · bloch-sphere-3d.tsx:92-93 - Scene receives `state` and only `target` is memoized (`useMemo(() =&gt; blochToThree(state), [state])`); the circle points and axis-line literals are not, so any new `state` array re-runs the whole Scene body · bloch-builder-widget.tsx:92 / wavefunction-scrubber.tsx:161 / scrolly-section.tsx:107 - all pass a freshly-computed `state` into &lt;BlochSphere3D&gt; on every drag/scrub/scroll update, driving the unmemoized re-renders) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-20 (WS-1) — ✓verified — NEW — **usePrefersReducedMotion getSnapshot allocates a MediaQueryList on every call**. The getSnapshot passed to useSyncExternalStore re-invokes window.matchMedia('(prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)') on every read, allocating a fresh MediaQueryList object each time just to read `.matches`. React calls getSnapshot on every render and after every store notification across all consumers (BlochBuilder, WavefunctionScrubber, ScrollySection). Because it returns a boolean primitive the value stays stable, so this is wasted allocation rather than a correctness bug, but it is on a hot path during scrubbing and scrolling. _Fix:_ In use-display-caps.ts, create one module-level MediaQueryList (`const reducedMq = window.matchMedia(...)` guarded for SSR) and have both subscribe and getSnapshot reference it, returning `reducedMq.matches`. This removes the per-read allocation while keeping the stable boolean snapshot. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (use-display-caps.ts:15 - getSnapshot is `() =&gt; window.matchMedia("(prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)").matches`, constructing a new MediaQueryList per call instead of reusing the one already created in the subscribe closure (line 11) · wavefunction-scrubber.tsx:44 and scrolly-section.tsx:143 - both call usePrefersReducedMotion(), and ScrollySection re-renders on every scroll rAF (progress state), so getSnapshot runs on each of those renders) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-20 (WS-1) — ✓verified (corrected 2026-06-20) — **useWebGL allocates a canvas + WebGL context on every render** (the part-1 refutation here was wrong). `useSyncExternalStore` calls getSnapshot (`detectWebGL`) on every render, not only on store change, and `detectWebGL` allocates a canvas + GL context each call; the consumers (this widget, wavefunction-scrubber, scrolly-section) re-render on drag/scrub/scroll, so GL contexts churn during interaction. See Feature 12 for the canonical entry + fix (memoize WebGL detection at module scope). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`use-display-caps.ts:20-27,29-36`) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Accessibility]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5a) — ✓verified — NEW — **ShotsSampler buttons lack the shared focus-ring and accessible labels**. Every other interactive control in this feature (sliders use .focus-ring, CorrelationDemo and the scrubber play button use `interactive focus-ring`, CopyButton uses them too) gets the project's high-contrast focus-visible ring. The ShotsSampler preset buttons and the Run button use none of those utilities, so they fall back to whatever the browser default outline is and visibly break the feature's focus-visibility consistency. The preset buttons also have no text beyond a bare number and no aria-label, and Run is unlabeled beyond its text. _Fix:_ In shots-sampler.tsx add `interactive focus-ring` to the preset buttons and Run button (matching CorrelationDemo's buttons), and give the preset buttons an aria-label like `aria-label={`${n} shots`}` since aria-pressed already conveys selection. Purely additive class/attribute change, no behavior change. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (shots-sampler.tsx:69-82 - preset buttons class list is `"rounded px-2.5 py-1 text-xs font-mono font-medium transition-colors"` plus selected/unselected colors, with no `focus-ring`/`interactive` · shots-sampler.tsx:83-88 - Run button class is `"ml-2 rounded px-3 py-1 text-xs font-semibold bg-accent text-white hover:bg-accent-dark transition-colors"`, no focus-ring · globals.css:262-268 - `.focus-ring` / `.interactive` utilities are the project-wide focus + press affordances applied by the other controls) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Accessibility]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5a) — ✓verified — NEW — **Range slider thumb is a 16px target, below the WCAG 2.5.8 minimum**. The shared .slider thumb (used by every theta/phi/scrub slider in the feature) is rendered at 16x16px on a 6px-tall track. WCAG 2.2 Success Criterion 2.5.8 (Target Size, Minimum) calls for at least 24x24 CSS px for pointer targets; a 16px draggable thumb on a thin rail is hard to grab on touch and for users with motor impairments. The sliders are keyboard-operable (so 2.5.8's exceptions partially apply), but the pointer affordance is undersized. _Fix:_ In globals.css enlarge the .slider thumb to at least 24x24px (or 20px thumb + a taller hit area via padding/`::-webkit-slider-runnable-track` height) for the webkit and moz thumb rules; this lifts every Foundations slider above the touch-target floor at once without touching component code. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (globals.css:274-283 - `.slider::-webkit-slider-thumb { width: 16px; height: 16px; ... }` · globals.css:284-292 - `.slider::-moz-range-thumb { width: 16px; height: 16px; ... }` · globals.css:271-273 - `.slider { @apply h-1.5 ... }` makes the track only 6px tall · bloch-builder-widget.tsx:111 / circuit-lab.tsx:118 / wavefunction-scrubber.tsx:193 - all sliders use `className="slider flex-1 focus-ring"`) — added 2026-06-20

- [x] **[Consistency & reuse]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-2b) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **Two Born-rule samplers exist for the same single-draw operation**. shots.ts `sampleCounts` and correlation.ts `sampleOutcome` both inverse-transform-sample a basis-state index from a `probs[]` array; `sampleCounts` does it n times with a binary-search CDF, `sampleOutcome` does one linear-scan draw. They are two implementations of the same Born-rule draw with divergent code (and `sampleCounts` builds its own CDF inline rather than reusing a shared single-draw primitive), so the sampling logic is maintained twice. _Fix:_ Define one `sampleIndex(cdf|probs, rng)` primitive (or have `sampleCounts` call `sampleOutcome` in a loop) in a single module (e.g. shots.ts) and have correlation.ts import it, so there is one Born-rule draw implementation. Keep `sampleCounts`'s batched CDF as the perf path that the single-draw helper shares. Coordinate with the zero-probability sampler fix so the consolidated primitive also skips zero-mass buckets. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (shots.ts:5-20 - `sampleCounts(probs,n,rng)` builds a CDF and binary-searches it n times to tally counts · correlation.ts:25-31 - `sampleOutcome(probs,rng)` linearly scans the same `probs` for one draw) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Consistency & reuse]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-2b) — ✓verified — NEW — **Two divergent angle-to-single-qubit-state functions with different amplitude conventions**. bloch-builder.ts `stateFromAngles(θ,φ)` returns cos(θ/2)|0⟩ + e^{iφ}sin(θ/2)|1⟩ (zero phase on |0⟩), while scrolly.ts `stateForAngles(θ,φ)` builds RZ(φ)·RY(θ)|0⟩, which carries a symmetric e^{∓iφ/2} global/relative phase split. Both map to the same Bloch vector (so the spheres agree), but they are two separate implementations of 'single-qubit state from Bloch angles' that produce different raw amplitude arrays — and only one feeds the copy-as-Python / Dirac readout, so the two declared sources of truth for this state can disagree on the literal amplitudes a learner copies. _Fix:_ Pick one canonical angle-to-state helper in a shared module (the math.ts kernel or bloch-builder.ts) and have both bloch-builder-widget and scrolly.ts import it, so the amplitude convention is single-sourced. If the RZ·RY phase split is intentional for the scrolly path, document why and still route both through one function with an explicit phase-convention flag. This is the same root cause as the BlochBuilder gate-chip mislabel correctness item — fixing one fixes both. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (bloch-builder.ts:4-11 - `stateFromAngles` returns `[c,0]` and `[s·cosφ, s·sinφ]` directly · scrolly.ts:61-66 - `stateForAngles` builds the state via `applyGate1(ry(theta))` then `applyGate1(rz(phi))` · bloch-builder-widget.tsx:29 - feeds `stateFromAngles(theta,phi)` into diracString/toPythonState copy buttons · scrolly.ts:68-70 - `stateForBeat` feeds `stateForAngles` into BlochDial via scrolly-section.tsx:54) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Consistency & reuse]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-2b) — ✓verified — NEW — **bloch-dial reimplements zeroState(1) and a unit-clamp the kernel could provide**. bloch-dial.tsx hand-declares `ZERO_STATE` as a literal `[[1,0],[0,0]]` default and a local `clampUnit` (Math.max(-1,Math.min(1,...))), while math.ts already exports `zeroState(n)` for the |0⟩ state and scrolly-section.tsx separately defines its own `clamp01`. The |0⟩ literal and the clamp helpers are small but re-declared rather than reused, so the dial's default state and the family's clamping live in their own copies. _Fix:_ Default `bloch-dial.tsx`'s `state` to `zeroState(1)` from math.ts instead of the local `ZERO_STATE`, and move a shared `clamp(v,min,max)` (or `clamp01`/`clampUnit`) into math.ts so bloch-dial.tsx and scrolly-section.tsx import one implementation. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (bloch-dial.tsx:3-7 - local `ZERO_STATE` literal and `clampUnit` helper · math.ts:65-69 - `zeroState(n)` already produces the |0⟩ state vector · scrolly-section.tsx:31 - a separate `clamp01` helper duplicating the same clamp idiom (also in scrolly.ts:82,96 inline)) — added 2026-06-20

> **Clean verification pass — 2026-06-20.** The adversarial verify stage that was server-throttled on the 2026-06-17 run completed cleanly here (22 findings survived independent skeptic review). _Current state:_ The noise math (Kraus channels, density-matrix conjugation, fidelity) and topology/cost logic are correct — no functional bugs surfaced this pass — and the issues are labeling clarity, accessibility (contrast, focus, touch targets), and DRY against cost.ts/math.ts as single sources of truth. The most consequential refinements are a WCAG-AA contrast bump on informational text, the device-table sort-button focus indicator (the largest reuse win), and deriving the device cost column from cost.ts so rates stop being maintained twice.

- [x] **[Accessibility — focus indicators & keyboard reachability]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-3) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **Device-table sort buttons have no keyboard focus indicator and no AT sort affordance**. The three sortable column-header buttons in device-table.tsx carry only hover and color-transition classes; they have no focus or focus-visible ring, so a keyboard or switch user tabbing through the table sees no indication of which header is focused — inconsistent with every other interactive control in the feature, where the sibling technology &lt;select&gt; (line 49) and the project `.focus-ring` utility (globals.css:262, used by topology-explorer and noise-visualizer) establish the focus-visible pattern. Additionally the buttons' accessible name is just the bare column word ('Model'/'Technology'/'Qubits') with the sort glyph aria-hidden, so they do not announce that they are sort controls. - [x] **[Consistency & reuse]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-2 tail) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **Device cost strings in devices.ts are a hand-maintained second copy of cost.ts rates**. cost.ts is declared 'single source of truth for rates' and holds the per-task/per-shot/per-minute numbers, yet every Cost cell in the device table comes from a hand-typed string literal in devices.ts (e.g. '$0.30/task + $0.01/shot', '$0.075/min'). - [x] **[Correctness]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5b) — ✓verified — NEW — **Qubit selector labels q1/q2 collide with 0-indexed qubit values shown beside them**. - [x] **[Correctness]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5b) — ✓verified — NEW — **All three noise channels share the label 'Error rate' though the parameter means different physical quantities**. The slider is labeled 'Error rate' and its value is announced as a single percentage for every channel, but the parameter p is a different physical quantity per channel: depolarizing uses the Pauli-error probability (capped at 0.75 where the qubit becomes maximally mixed), amplitude-damping uses gamma (the relaxation/decay probability, max 1.0), and bit-flip uses the flip probability (max 1.0). A learner switching channels sees the same 'Error rate %' wording even though, e.g., depolarizing 'maxes out' at 75% while the others reach 100%, which can imply the depolarizing slider is broken or that 75% is a generic error ceiling. _Fix:_ In noise-visualizer.tsx make the slider label channel-aware (e.g. 'Depolarizing p', 'Damping γ', 'Flip probability') or add a one-line caption noting that depolarizing reaches the maximally-mixed state at p=0.75 while the others run to 1.0. No math change — noise.ts is correct; only the visible labeling needs to stop conflating the three quantities. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (noise-visualizer.tsx:178 - the label is the generic string `Error rate` for all channels · noise-visualizer.tsx:31 - pMax is 0.75 for depolarizing but 1 for the others, so the same 'Error rate' tops out at different values without explanation · noise.ts:79-90 - krausFor treats p as Pauli-error prob (depolarizing), gamma (amplitude-damping), and flip prob (bit-flip) — three distinct quantities under one UI label) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance / UX — busy feedback]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5b) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **Noise slider re-runs the full Kraus density-matrix simulation synchronously on every drag tick with no busy feedback**. The error-rate slider's onChange calls setP directly on every input event, and pClamped is a dependency of the rho useMemo, which calls noisyRho() — a full density-matrix Kraus-channel simulation (two 2^n x 2^n matrix multiplies per gate plus one per Kraus operator per qubit). With step=0.01 and a max of 0.75-1.0, dragging the slider fires 75-100 discrete React state updates, each forcing a synchronous main-thread recompute and re-render before paint, with no debounce, useDeferredValue, startTransition, or rAF throttle anywhere in the file — and no pending/busy indication, so on a multi-gate circuit the bars and fidelity readout can lag the thumb. (Because n is hard-capped at 3, d≤8, so per-tick cost is small in absolute terms; user-visible lag is realistically Low except on unusually long circuits.) _Fix:_ In noise-visualizer.tsx, decouple the slider's visual value from the simulated value: keep `p` immediate for the thumb/label but feed a throttled/deferred value (useDeferredValue, a startTransition in onChange, or a requestAnimationFrame-coalesced value) into the rho/noisy/fidelity memos so at most one simulation runs per frame and the thumb stays responsive. Optionally add a transient busy affordance (lower bar opacity or aria-busy on the bars container) while a recompute is pending. Keep idealState/ideal memos as-is (they correctly exclude p). No scope change — same simulation, same math. Impact: Low. Effort: Medium. (noise-visualizer.tsx:187 - slider onChange does `setP(parseFloat(e.target.value))` with no deferral/debounce/rAF throttle · noise-visualizer.tsx:42-45 - `rho` useMemo lists `pClamped` in its deps, so it re-runs noisyRho on every p change, synchronously in render · noise-visualizer.tsx:185 - `step={0.01}` means a full-track drag emits ~75-100 onChange events · noise.ts:109-123 - noisyRho loops over ops doing conjugate(U, rho) (two matMul, each O(d^3)) plus applyChannel1 per qubit; grep confirms no requestAnimationFrame/useDeferredValue/startTransition/debounce in the component · noise.ts:30-40 - matMul is a triple-nested O(d^3) complex multiply with no memo cache across slider ticks) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-4 perf) — ✓verified — NEW — **krausFor() recomputed once per gate inside noisyRho even though it is loop-invariant for a fixed (channel, p)**. Inside noisyRho the per-op loop recomputes `const kraus = krausFor(channel, p)` on every gate, but the Kraus operator set depends only on (channel, p) and is identical for every op in a single call. For the live 2-gate qnoise block this is 2x redundant; the redundancy scales with circuit length. Each krausFor call allocates fresh Gate2 arrays (scaleGate builds new nested arrays), so this is needless allocation churn on the same drag-tick hot path as the simulation above. _Fix:_ In noise.ts hoist `const kraus = p &gt; 0 ? krausFor(channel, p) : null;` to before the op loop in noisyRho and reuse it inside the loop. This is a pure loop-invariant code motion within the existing function — no behavior change. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (noise.ts:114-121 - the `for (const op of ops)` loop computes `const kraus = krausFor(channel, p)` at line 118 inside the loop body, only used when p &gt; 0 · noise.ts:79-91 - krausFor allocates new Gate2 arrays per call (scaleGate at line 72-77 builds fresh nested arrays each invocation)) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-4 perf) — ✓verified — NEW — **expandSingle rebuilds identity(2) matrices for every Kraus operator on every gate during each noisy recompute**. applyChannel1 calls conjugate(expandSingle(k, qubit, n), rho) for each of up to 4 Kraus operators per affected qubit per gate. expandSingle (noise.ts:53-57) rebuilds the full 2^n x 2^n expansion from scratch via repeated kron, allocating a fresh identity(2) for each non-target slot every call. For depolarizing on a 2-qubit CNOT this is 2 qubits x 4 Kraus x n kron-builds-with-fresh-identities, all redone on every slider tick, and identity(2) is a constant that never changes. _Fix:_ In noise.ts hoist a module-level `const I2_MAT = identity(2)` and reference it in expandSingle's kron instead of calling identity(2) inline; this removes one allocation per non-target slot per Kraus operator per gate without changing results. (Optional further refinement: the per-qubit single-channel superoperator is constant for a fixed (channel, p, qubit, n) and could be cached, but the identity hoist is the low-risk, in-scope win.) Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (noise.ts:93-96 - applyChannel1 loops kraus calling expandSingle then conjugate (two matMul) for each operator · noise.ts:53-57 - expandSingle calls `kron(res, q === qubit ? gate2ToMatrix(g) : identity(2))` building a new identity(2) per slot, per call · noise.ts:15-19 - identity() allocates a fresh d x d array (here always identity(2)) on every invocation, with no memoization) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-4 perf) — ✓verified — NEW — **TopologyGraph rebuilds the full edge list outside useMemo while adjacent derivations are memoized**. Inside TopologyGraph, positions, adjacency, and the path-edge set are each wrapped in useMemo, but the `edges` array — an O(E) reconstruction that for all-to-all with the 16-qubit max is 16*15/2 = 120 edge objects — is built as plain code in the render body on every render, then filtered twice (.filter !highlighted and .filter highlighted) to map. It only re-renders on discrete select changes so this is not a per-frame hot loop, but it is an unmemoized allocation inconsistent with the surrounding memoized values and trivially hoistable. _Fix:_ In topology-explorer.tsx wrap the edges construction in a useMemo keyed on [positions, adj, pathEdgeSet, n] so it only recomputes when its inputs change, matching the existing memoization pattern in the same component. Optionally partition into faintEdges/pathEdges once inside that memo to drop the two per-render .filter passes. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (topology-explorer.tsx:167-177 - `const edges: {...}[] = []` is built in the render body (nested loop over n and adj[u]), not in a useMemo, unlike positions (line 149), adj (line 154), and pathEdgeSet (line 157) · topology-explorer.tsx:192-221 - edges is then iterated twice via .filter().map() each render, allocating two intermediate arrays) — added 2026-06-20

- [x] **[UX — input editing friction]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5b) — ✓verified — NEW — **Cost-calculator number inputs coerce empty/partial entry to 1 on each keystroke, fighting the user mid-edit**. The Tasks, Shots, and Minutes inputs all run `Math.max(1, Math.round(Number(e.target.value)))` directly in onChange. Clearing the field to retype (empty string -&gt; Number('')===0 -&gt; max(1,0)===1) snaps the value back to 1 instantly, so a user cannot blank the field to type a new number and a backspace-to-edit flow is interrupted on every keystroke, which reads as the control fighting the user. _Fix:_ In cost-calculator.tsx, allow a transient empty/partial value while typing and clamp to the &gt;=1 floor on blur (or only clamp when the parsed value is a finite number), so editing the field is not interrupted. The clamp still guarantees a valid value for `estimateCost`. Refine the existing inputs only. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. - [x] **[UI & cleaner code]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5b) — ✓verified — NEW — **Topology SVG carries dead width/height attributes that the className overrides**. The TopologyGraph &lt;svg&gt; sets both explicit `width={SVG_W} height={SVG_H}` (300x200) and `className="w-full max-w-xs mx-auto block"`. Tailwind's `w-full` always wins over the width attribute, so the rendered width is governed by CSS and the explicit width/height attributes are inert — the viewBox alone preserves the aspect ratio. They read as load-bearing sizing but do nothing. _Fix:_ In topology-explorer.tsx drop the `width`/`height` attributes from the &lt;svg&gt; (keep them only in the viewBox string and geometry math) so the sizing is unambiguously CSS-driven; optionally keep `height` if a fixed pixel height is wanted, but not a width that w-full negates. - [x] **[Consistency & reuse]** DONE 2026-06-21 (already resolved in #19: widget uses stateFidelity + noisyRho; fidelityDist kept as a tested teaching utility) — ✓verified — NEW — **noise-visualizer.tsx re-derives noisy probabilities inline instead of the existing noisyProbs, and exports noisyProbs/fidelityDist are UI-dead**. noise.ts exports noisyProbs(ops,n,channel,p) — which returns exactly the density-matrix diagonal as a probability vector and is covered by noise.test.ts — but the widget ignores it: it calls noisyRho itself and then re-extracts the diagonal by hand with `rho.map((row, i) =&gt; row[i][0])` (the verbatim body of noisyProbs). It also exports fidelityDist (squared Bhattacharyya), but the UI uses true stateFidelity, not the classical overlap. So both exports are dead from the feature's UI perspective (referenced only by tests) and the widget duplicates noisyProbs' one-liner rather than reusing it. (Note: the widget legitimately still needs the full rho for stateFidelity, so the cleanest fix may be a shared diagOf(rho) helper rather than calling noisyProbs.) _Fix:_ Either route the widget through noisyProbs / a shared diagOf(rho) helper to remove the hand-rolled diagonal extraction at noise-visualizer.tsx:46, or keep these as deliberately-tested public utilities and add a one-line comment in noise.ts noting they are exercised by tests / external callers, not the widget; if fidelityDist is meant only for the widget, drop it (the UI uses true stateFidelity, not the classical overlap). Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (noise.ts:126-128 - `export function noisyProbs(...) { return noisyRho(...).map((row, i) =&gt; row[i][0]); }` · noise.ts:150-155 - `export function fidelityDist(...)` (squared Bhattacharyya), never imported by the widget · noise-visualizer.tsx:6 - imports only `noisyRho, stateFidelity`; noise-visualizer.tsx:46 - `const noisy = useMemo(() =&gt; rho.map((row, i) =&gt; row[i][0]), [rho])` inlines noisyProbs' logic · __tests__/components/quantum/noise.test.ts:13-37 - noisyProbs is exercised by tests but never imported by the production widget (no usages of noisyProbs in src/ outside noise.ts); noise-visualizer.tsx:80 uses stateFidelity rather than fidelityDist) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Consistency & reuse]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-2 tail) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **noise.ts opMatrix duplicates the gate-name→matrix dispatch already in math.ts (NAMED_GATES is private)**. noise.ts opMatrix hand-writes a string-to-Gate2 chain — `g === "RX" ? rx(...) : g === "RY" ? ry(...) : ... : g === "H" ? H : g === "S" ? S : g === "T" ? T : I2` — that resolves the same gate set math.ts applyOp resolves via its NAMED_GATES record plus the rx/ry/rz branch. The application targets differ (opMatrix builds a full operator for density-matrix conjugation; applyOp acts on a state vector), but the gate-lookup table itself is identical and maintained twice. math.ts keeps NAMED_GATES private, so noise.ts cannot reuse the canonical table even though it wants the exact same mapping. _Fix:_ Export from math.ts a single gate-resolution primitive — either NAMED_GATES, or a `gateMatrixFor(op: Op): Gate2` that handles named gates + rx/ry/rz (throwing for CNOT) — and have noise.ts opMatrix call it for the single-qubit case, keeping only its CNOT/expandCNOT logic local. - [x] **[Consistency & reuse]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5b) — ✓verified — NEW — **SWAP-count formula is duplicated between swapCost and topology-explorer's graph aria-label**. topology.ts swapCost already computes `swaps: Math.max(0, path.length - 2)` and returns it, and the main component consumes that returned value. But TopologyGraph independently recomputes the identical expression `const swaps = Math.max(0, path.length - 2)` solely to build its aria-label, instead of being passed the swaps value the parent already has. ### 8. Algorithms explorables

- [x] **[Correctness]** ✓verified — **QFT visualizer asserts a false "spikes every N/r" claim for periods that don't divide N**: `spacing=N/value` is accepted without a divisibility check, so period 3 / N 8 prints "spikes every N/r = 2.6666666666666665" and `idx % spacing` (fractional) highlights only bin 0. > **Clean verification pass — 2026-06-20.** The adversarial verify stage that was server-throttled on the 2026-06-17 run completed cleanly here (4 findings survived independent skeptic review). _Current state:_ The QAOA and Deutsch-Jozsa simulations are numerically correct (the cut math is endian-agnostic and validated), so this feature has no functional bugs — the one correctness item is a pedagogical labeling mirror-image, not a math error. The headline opportunity is performance: QAOA simulates the full state vector twice per slider tick and recomputes graph-only quantities (maxCut, the cut-value table) far more than necessary, all of which are clean refinements of the existing kernel.

- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-4) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **QAOA simulates the full state vector twice and recomputes the graph-only maxCut on every gamma/beta slider tick**. The `live` memo recomputes on every gamma/beta change and calls both `qaoaExpectedCut(n, edges, gamma, beta)` and `qaoaDistribution(n, edges, gamma, beta)`. `qaoaExpectedCut` internally calls `qaoaDistribution`, which calls `qaoaState` (allocates a 2^n complex array, computes the cost phase via cutValue over all 2^n states, then applies n single-qubit gates each re-cloning the state). So the entire state-vector simulation runs twice per tick to produce two values (expected cut and distribution) that come from one identical state. The same memo also recomputes `maxCut` by looping all 2^n basis states and calling cutValue on each, even though maxCut depends only on the graph and never changes when gamma/beta move. _Fix:_ In qaoa-explorer.tsx, simulate once per tick: compute `const dist = qaoaDistribution(n, edges, gamma, beta)` and derive `expected` from `dist` (sum dist[x]*cut[x]) instead of calling qaoaExpectedCut, which removes the second qaoaState run. Move the `maxCut` loop out of the gamma/beta `live` memo into its own memo keyed on `[parsed]` (it is graph-only, like `landscape`/`gridMax`). Optionally add a `qaoaExpectedFromDistribution(dist, cuts)` helper in qaoa.ts so expected and distribution share one state vector. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (qaoa-explorer.tsx:229 - `const expected = qaoaExpectedCut(n, edges, gamma, beta);` · qaoa-explorer.tsx:230 - `const distribution = qaoaDistribution(n, edges, gamma, beta);` (second independent full simulation of the same state) · qaoa.ts:35-39 - `qaoaExpectedCut` calls `qaoaDistribution(...)` then loops cutValue over all 2^n states; `qaoaDistribution` (qaoa.ts:31-33) calls `qaoaState`, so each call is a full sim · qaoa.ts:19-29 - `qaoaState` allocates `new Array(N)`, runs cutValue per basis state, then applyGate1 n times (each cloning the whole state vector) · qaoa-explorer.tsx:232 - `for (let x = 0; x &lt; 1 &lt;&lt; n; x++) maxCut = Math.max(maxCut, cutValue(x, edges));` runs inside the gamma/beta-dependent `live` memo despite being graph-only · qaoa-explorer.tsx:234 - `}, [parsed, gamma, beta]);` so all of the above re-runs every slider tick) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Correctness]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-4) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **QAOA distribution bitstrings are reversed relative to the graph's vertex numbering**. qaoa.ts maps graph vertex i to bit position i via (x&gt;&gt;i)&amp;1 (LSB-indexed), so vertex 0 is the least-significant bit of the basis index. The distribution bars and the SVG graph are both labeled, but basisLabel renders the index MSB-first (qubit 0 leftmost), so the leftmost character of a bar label is vertex n-1 and the rightmost is vertex 0. A learner reading a bar label like |0001&gt; left-to-right as vertices 0,1,2,3 concludes 'vertex 3 is in the cut set' when the math actually places vertex 0 there — the partition shown by the bars is mirror-imaged versus the numbered nodes in GraphSvg. _Fix:_ Make the bar labels read in vertex order so they match the numbered nodes in GraphSvg. In qaoa-explorer.tsx, render the distribution label by reversing the bit order relative to basisLabel (e.g. build the per-vertex string as bits v0 v1 ... v(n-1) from (idx&gt;&gt;v)&amp;1), and/or add a short caption stating the read direction (left = vertex 0). Alternatively, flip cutValue/the vertex-to-bit mapping in qaoa.ts to use bit (n-1-i) so vertex i lines up with basisLabel's i-th character — but the explorer-side fix is lower-risk since it leaves the validated cut math untouched. Keep GraphSvg vertex numbering as the single source of truth. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (qaoa.ts:7 - cutValue uses ((x &gt;&gt; i) &amp; 1) so vertex i is bit position i (LSB-indexed, vertex 0 = least-significant bit) · math.ts:191-193 - basisLabel(i,n) returns i.toString(2).padStart(n,'0'), i.e. MSB-first with the most-significant bit (qubit 0 per the file's stated big-endian convention) as the leftmost character · qaoa-explorer.tsx:371 - each distribution bar is labeled |{basisLabel(idx, n)}&gt; with no reversal of the per-vertex reading order · qaoa-explorer.tsx:165 - GraphSvg prints the literal vertex index {i} on each node, so the displayed graph numbers vertices 0..n-1 left/around while the bar string runs vertex (n-1)..0 · /tmp/qaoa_check.mjs run - star graph edges [[0,1],[0,2],[0,3]], the cut=3 optimum 'vertex0 isolated' is index 1 which basisLabel renders '0001' (vertex 0 is the rightmost char, not leftmost)) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-4) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **QAOA landscape recomputes the immutable cut-value table for all 2^n states on every grid cell instead of once per graph**. `qaoaLandscape` builds a RES x RES = 576-cell grid, calling `qaoaExpectedCut` for each cell. Every one of those 576 calls runs `qaoaState` (which recomputes cutValue for all 2^n basis states to build the cost phase) and then loops cutValue again over all 2^n states for the expectation. The per-basis-state cut values depend only on the graph, not on gamma/beta, so the same cut[x] table is reconstructed from scratch ~1152 times for a single graph. The landscape memo only runs once per graph so this is not a per-tick cost, but it is O(cells * 2^n * edges) redundant work that dominates first paint / graph-change time. _Fix:_ In qaoa.ts, precompute `cuts[x] = cutValue(x, edges)` once for x in 0..2^n-1 and thread that array through `qaoaState`, `qaoaExpectedCut`, and `qaoaLandscape` (e.g. build `cuts` once at the top of `qaoaLandscape` and pass it down). This collapses ~1152 cutValue table builds into one per graph, with no behavioral change. Impact: Low. Effort: Medium. (qaoa.ts:43-55 - `qaoaLandscape` nests `res` x `res` loops, each iteration calling `qaoaExpectedCut(n, edges, gamma, beta)` · qaoa.ts:6-10 - `cutValue` loops over all edges for one basis state; it is called for every x in qaoaState (qaoa.ts:24) and again in qaoaExpectedCut (qaoa.ts:38) · qaoa-explorer.tsx:23 - `const RES = 24;` so the landscape is 24*24 = 576 cells, each triggering two full cutValue passes over 2^n states · qaoa-explorer.tsx:200-203 - landscape memo (`[parsed]`) builds the whole grid; the cut table is identical across all 576 cells but never cached) — added 2026-06-20
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-4 perf) — ✓verified — NEW — **applyGate1 clones the entire state vector on every gate application in the QAOA/DJ kernels**. `applyGate1` starts by `state.map((c) =&gt; [...])` to allocate a fresh output array of N complex pairs, then overwrites every entry. QAOA's mixer applies it n times per state (qaoa.ts:27) and the DJ circuit applies it 2n times (deutsch-jozsa.ts:24,26), so each simulation allocates n (or 2n) throwaway 2^n-length arrays plus 2^n nested two-element arrays. For QAOA this is multiplied by the 576-cell landscape build and by the twice-per-tick live sim, turning gate application into the dominant allocation source for this feature. _Fix:_ In math.ts, give applyGate1 an in-place butterfly variant (or reuse a single scratch buffer) so each gate mutates the existing pair of indices rather than cloning the whole vector; only the (i, j) pair per stride is touched, so a full clone is unnecessary. This is shared infrastructure used by every algorithm widget here, so the win compounds across QAOA landscape, DJ, and the live sims. Keep the existing non-mutating signature for external callers if needed. Impact: Low. Effort: Medium. (math.ts:72-84 - `applyGate1` does `const out = state.map((c) =&gt; [c[0], c[1]] as Complex);` allocating a full N-entry array of new pairs before the butterfly loop overwrites them · qaoa.ts:27 - `for (let q = 0; q &lt; n; q++) state = applyGate1(state, rx(2 * beta), q, n);` allocates a new array per qubit · deutsch-jozsa.ts:24 - `for (let q = 0; q &lt; n; q++) state = applyGate1(state, H, q, n);` (and again at deutsch-jozsa.ts:26) doubles the allocations per DJ run) — added 2026-06-20

- [x] **[UI]** DONE 2026-06-21 (WS-5c: dropped CSS transitions on marker/dropline; added theta x-axis ticks; floor label anchors the energy min) — ✓verified — confirms prior — **VQE optimizer trace rubber-bands and the plot has no axis scale**. The optimizer animates with `setTimeout(tick, ANIM_MS=32)` (~31 fps) while the trace marker and lines use CSS `transition-[cx,cy] duration-150`, so each 32ms position update restarts a 150ms ease the next frame interrupts — the marker visibly lags/rubber-bands during Optimize. The energy/θ plot also has only caption text, no numeric axis ticks/scale, so values are unanchored. _Fix:_ drop the CSS transition during animation (let the 32ms steps drive motion) or raise `ANIM_MS` to ≥150ms; add min/mid/max axis ticks. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. > **Re-confirmed 2026-06-20** by direct source review. CORRECTION: the part-1 workflow's F6 pass *incorrectly refuted* the useWebGL per-render allocation; direct review confirms it is REAL — `useSyncExternalStore` calls getSnapshot on every render, and `detectWebGL` allocates a canvas + GL context each call.

- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-20 (WS-1) — ✓verified (corrected 2026-06-20) — **useWebGL allocates a canvas + WebGL context on every render of every consumer**. useWebGL's getSnapshot is `detectWebGL`, which does `document.createElement("canvas")` + `getContext("webgl2")||getContext("webgl")` each call; React invokes getSnapshot on every render (not only on store change), and the consumers — bloch-builder-widget, wavefunction-scrubber, scrolly-section — re-render on slider drag / scrub-play / scroll rAF, so a fresh GL context is created and discarded many times per second during interaction (browsers also cap live GL contexts, risking context-loss churn). _Fix:_ memoize WebGL detection at module scope (compute once; return the cached boolean from both subscribe and getSnapshot). The sibling `usePrefersReducedMotion` has the same per-call `matchMedia` allocation (see Feature 6). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`use-display-caps.ts:20-27` detectWebGL allocates canvas+GL · `:29-36` useWebGL passes detectWebGL as getSnapshot with a no-op subscribe · callers bloch-builder-widget.tsx / wavefunction-scrubber.tsx / scrolly-section.tsx all re-render hot) — added 2026-06-17
- [x] **[Architecture & consistency]** DONE 2026-06-21 (gate set in WS-2 tail #39; ParsedGate.angle renamed to theta so the parsed and runtime ops share one field — WS-5d) — ✓verified (re-confirmed 2026-06-20) — **qsim gate set + op types are double-sourced**. The gate name set lives twice — `math.ts` NAMED_GATES (I,X,Y,Z,H,S,T):60 + the RX/RY/RZ branch in applyOp:131, vs `qsim-dsl.ts` SINGLE:34 / ROT:35 — and the parsed vs runtime op shapes diverge (`ParsedGate.angle` qsim-dsl.ts:23 vs `Op.theta` math.ts:121, bridged by `opsFor`). (`math.ts:60,131` vs `qsim-dsl.ts:34-35` · `ParsedGate.angle` qsim-dsl.ts:23 vs `Op.theta` math.ts:121 · `bloch-builder.ts:4-17` hand-rolled state) — added 2026-06-17

- [x] **[UI · correctness]** DONE 2026-06-25 (WS-6a, PR #60 merged) — **`diracString` prints "+ -0.71" for negative amplitudes** — it joins every term with the literal `"  +  "` with no per-term sign handling, while `formatAmplitude` can return a leading `-`. This is the headline teaching output of every circuit-family explorable (`StateReadout`) and hits very common states: H then Z gives `0.71|0⟩  +  -0.71|1⟩`, and |Φ⁻⟩ shows the same artifact. Make `diracString` sign-aware (emit magnitude, assemble with `" - "`/`" + "`; first term keeps a bare leading minus). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. _New cross-feature findings (2026-06-25 deep audit — the four sweeps that a per-feature reviewer structurally cannot see):_

## Category C — features 13-33 (analyzed 2026-06-17, big multi-agent run)

> 85 reviewer findings recovered from a rate-limited run (verify stage throttled).
> Items below are tagged ✓verified (re-read in code: 4 inline + `estimate_cost` by
> the workflow) or ~reviewer (file:line evidence, pending a clean verification pass).
> Long tail of Medium/Low items lives in the run transcripts.

### 13-14. In-browser execution runtime
- [ ] **[Resilience]** ✓verified — **No execution timeout**: `runSerialized` awaits `runPythonAsync` with no timeout/abort on a shared module-global queue, so a learner's `while True: pass` hangs the tab AND wedges every subsequent run/grade (the reject-guard only handles errors, not hangs). **DEFERRED**: a JS `Promise.race` cannot interrupt a CPU-bound `while True` (Pyodide blocks the main thread, so `setTimeout` never fires) — the real fix is moving the runtime to a Web Worker (its own PR). Impact: High. Effort: High. (`web/src/lib/pyodide-runtime.ts:70,84-95`) — added 2026-06-17
- [x] **[Resilience]** ✓verified — DONE (PR pending) — **A failed Pyodide boot is cached forever**: `getPyodide` assigns `pyodidePromise` before the async boot and returns it unconditionally, so one CDN/wheel failure bricks every runnable cell with no retry. Null the cache on rejection. Impact: High. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/pyodide-runtime.ts:46-64`) — added 2026-06-17
- [ ] **[Correctness]** ~reviewer — stderr is mislabeled as successful stdout in the runnable editor; the stdout/stderr sink is never detached after a run, leaking async output into the next run. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`runnable-editor.tsx`, `pyodide-runtime.ts:84-95`) — added 2026-06-17
- [ ] **[Performance/Consistency]** ~reviewer — every runnable fence eagerly mounts its own Monaco editor on hydration (no viewport gating); qcsim bootstrap is triplicated across 3 authored copies; Pyodide version pinned independently in TS runtime + JupyterLite kernel (driftable). Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`runnable-editor.tsx`, `pyodide-runtime.ts:12`, `jupyterlite-build/`) — added 2026-06-17
- [ ] **[Accessibility]** ~reviewer — run success/error conveyed only by an aria-hidden color dot; disabled "Run in browser" button unreachable by keyboard/SR. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`runnable-editor.tsx`, `notebook-link.tsx`) — added 2026-06-17
- **[Boundary note — not a refinement]** 2026-07-17: the JupyterLite lab remains the one execution surface with no path into the mastery loop — `notebook-link.tsx:70-78` opens `/lab/lab/index.html` in a new tab, and `web/public/lab/` contains zero host-facing `postMessage`/`BroadcastChannel` wiring (the Pyodide kernel runs in a worker, which has no `localStorage`). Wiring lab outcomes to `gradeCard()` would require a custom JupyterLite extension — new plumbing, out of scope for `/optimize-features`. The in-scope route to graded notebook skills is the `tier:"py"` item under `### 15`.

### 15. Code challenge auto-grader
- [x] **[Correctness]** ✓verified — DONE (PR pending) — **Slider-bound `theta` in a target program grades against the wrong state**: both graders build the reference via `opsFor(target, 0)`, so a `theta` rotation in the author's `target.program` collapses to RY(0)=identity. Reject reference programs with `hasTheta === true`. Impact: High. Effort: Low. (`challenge-grade.ts:38`, `pyodide-grader.ts:53`, `qsim-dsl.ts:71-73,102`) — added 2026-06-17

FIXED: `MAX_QUBITS` clamp at both grader entries (`challenge-grade.ts`, `pyodide-grader.ts`); parse-error guard added in #21. RECLASSIFIED by the security audit to **author-only / Low** — the learner path is already hard-clamped at `MAX_QUBITS=4` (`qsim-dsl.ts:91`), so this is defense-in-depth against an author typo, not a learner-triggerable DoS. Impact: High→Low. Effort: Low. — added 2026-06-17
- [ ] **[Accessibility]** ~reviewer — the verdict `role="status"` region is conditionally mounted, so SR misses the announcement; add `aria-live` always-present. Impact: High. Effort: Low. (`challenge.tsx:168-175`) — added 2026-06-17
- [ ] **[Security/Tests]** ~reviewer (RECLASSIFIED + DEFERRED) — Tier-B `gradePy` raw-Python concat. Security audit verdict: **not a security vuln** — Pyodide is the learner's own same-user WASM sandbox, so "injection" self-harms only. Residual is grading-INTEGRITY (a learner can false-pass by stubbing `circuit`) — Low, and only matters once `tier:"py"` content ships (none today; cross-run leakage already prevented by the fresh per-run namespace). DEFERRED: namespace the grading epilogue away from learner symbols. The "no SRI on the Pyodide/Monaco CDN" half is promoted to its own audit finding below. Impact: Low. Effort: Medium. (`pyodide-grader.ts`) — added 2026-06-17
- [ ] **[Security]** PARTIAL 2026-06-25 — ✓verified (audit 2026-06-18, re-verified 2026-06-25). **DONE (PR #56/#58):** the Pyodide half is closed — the lesson runtime and lab kernel are now self-hosted SAME-ORIGIN (`/pyodide/`, `/lab/`) as the primary path, with the jsdelivr fallback carrying SRI + `crossorigin` on the bootstrap script (`web/src/lib/pyodide-runtime.ts:18-32,53-66`). **STILL OPEN:** (1) **Monaco** still loads its editor core from a CDN with no SRI — `@monaco-editor/react` fetches it on first mount (`web/src/components/code-editor.tsx:13-25`), so a tampered Monaco CDN still executes with full page privileges; (2) there is **no site-wide CSP** to backstop either loader (`customHttp.yml` carries only cache headers — see the Feature 31 item in the 27-33 tail). Fix: self-host or pin+SRI Monaco, and ship a CSP via a staged report-only rollout. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/code-editor.tsx:13-25`, `customHttp.yml`) — added 2026-06-18, narrowed 2026-06-25
- [x] **[Architecture & UX]** CLOSED 2026-07-17 (PR #167, c637988) — **The Tier-B Python grader is fully built and wired — and zero shipped content uses it** — `gradePy` runs learner Braket-style Python in the same-origin Pyodide worker and compares state vectors up to global phase, and its solve verdict flows through the same `apply()` → `gradeCardIfDue` path as Tier A (`challenge.tsx:155-156,138`), but no `qchallenge` fence anywhere sets `tier:"py"` (the only mount is the unlinked `/e2e-fixtures/py-challenge`) and `rep-schema.ts:19-22` rejects the tier outright because CI cannot exercise the Pyodide path. This is the highest-leverage rail for grading notebook-exercise responses: author `tier:"py"` Reps in the lesson pages that mirror the notebook exercises' target skills, so real Python answers get graded and land in the existing per-user mastery loop (FSRS card → `qc:*` sync → bench/records) with no new machinery. Prerequisites: extend the Playwright e2e suite (which already boots real Pyodide) with a grading assertion per shipped py Rep so the rep-schema gate can be relaxed honestly, and close the deferred grading-integrity item first (namespace the grading epilogue away from learner symbols in `pyodide-grader.ts`). Impact: High. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/quantum/challenge.tsx:136-148,155-168`, `web/src/lib/pyodide-grader.ts:29-88`, `web/src/lib/rep-schema.ts:19-22`) — added 2026-07-17

The drift is load-bearing because the cost gate is fail-open — see new item **24.a** below — so collapsing to one table also closes that safety hole.)_
- [x] **[Correctness/Tests]** DONE (PR pending) — `parse_counts` assumed bitstring column position == qubit index. FIXED: documents the contract and raises if `result.measured_qubits` is exposed and isn't `0..n-1` in order (rather than silently mislabeling); + a column-order pin test and a non-contiguous-rejection test. (The audit cleared the *web* qjw visualizer — its column==qubit is a correct big-endian convention, not a bug.) Remaining sub-items (mock-dtype divergence, GHZ-coverage, half-typed API) are separate, still open. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`lib/utils/results.py`) — added 2026-06-17

> **Category E (`lib/`, Features 21–25) — deep refinement pass (2026-06-29).** A dynamic
> workflow ran 23 read-only reviews (5 features × 4 per-feature lenses — Cleaner code,
> Performance, Resilience & tests, Security — plus 3 lib-wide sweeps for Architecture,
> Consistency, and Observability & cost), then adversarially verified every finding
> (file:line real on `main`? a refinement not a new feature? already handled? impact honest?).
> **61 candidates → 58 confirmed, 3 rejected** (a wrong line-cite, the intentional local-path
> shots design, and an over-claimed observability item). The verifier corrected **every**
> claimed-High down to Medium/Low — `lib/` is genuinely strong (tight modules, honest docstrings,
> fail-loud validation, real local-simulator tests), so the result is **4 Medium** items and the
> rest Low, with heavy cross-lens duplication folded here (the cost-gate fail-open surfaced under
> 5 lenses; the H2/LiH builder duplication under 3; the `quantum_kernel` qubit-count bug under 2).
> This pass **sharpens** three still-open 2026-06-17 items rather than duplicating them: the
> device-registry unification (updated in place above), the `quantum_kernel` fresh-`LocalSimulator`
> per call (remains tracked under `### 22-23` above — verified real but its O(N²) Gram amplification
> is hypothetical: no Gram-matrix builder exists in the repo), and the `train_vqc` double-pass
> (superseded by the sharper batching fix, item **23.a**). The new per-feature items below are
> the distinct, file:line-grounded refinements.

### 21. Circuit primitives
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-29 (added `test_qft_circuit_matches_analytic_dft`: prepares `|k=1>`, compares the shots=0 statevector to the analytic DFT via a global-phase-/convention-robust fidelity, plus a non-trivial-imaginary check. Teeth-verified — a phase-stripped QFT scores fidelity 0.43 and fails. Kept the uniform-on-`|000>` sanity test.) — QFT correctness test is degenerate — measures `qft_circuit(3)` on `|000>` and asserts a roughly-uniform histogram, but the QFT of *any* basis state is uniform, so a Hadamard-only circuit (all phases/swaps deleted) passes identically; the Fourier structure is effectively untested. Fix: compare the statevector on a non-trivial `|k≠0>` against the analytic DFT amplitudes (the own-adjoint round-trip is itself degenerate — `c·c†=I` for any unitary). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`tests/test_circuits.py:40-50`, `lib/circuits/common.py:36-39`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-29 (both tests now also assert each branch occurs in a 0.35–0.65 band of 1000 shots via `measurement_counts`. Teeth-verified — a dropped Hadamard collapses the state and the new assertions fail.) — Bell/GHZ tests assert correlation only — `row[0]==row[1]` / all-bits-agree pass vacuously on the collapsed product state `|00…0>` (a dropped Hadamard, no superposition/entanglement). Also assert both branches occur (all-zeros and all-ones each in a ~35–65% band; Binomial std ≈1.6% at 1000 shots, safe). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`tests/test_circuits.py:12-13,26-27`, `lib/circuits/common.py:13,24`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-30 (P1, PR pending — `ghz_state`/`qft_circuit` raise `ValueError("n_qubits must be >= 1")`; `bell_pair` raises `ValueError("... must be distinct")`; `pytest.raises` tests added) — Degenerate inputs accepted silently — `ghz_state(0)`/`ghz_state(-3)` return a 1-qubit circuit (the `h(0)` is unconditional) and `qft_circuit(0)`/`(-3)` an empty one, while `bell_pair(2,2)` leaks an opaque Braket target-set ValueError. Add `n_qubits >= 1` guards and a `qubit_0 != qubit_1` guard with teachable messages + `pytest.raises` tests. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/circuits/common.py:14,24-25,38`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Cleaner code]** DONE 2026-06-30 (P1, PR pending — `qft_circuit` docstring now documents `n_qubits` and the trailing bit-reversal swap, with an inline comment on the swap loop) — `qft_circuit` docstring is thinner than its siblings and omits the non-obvious final-swap behavior — `bell_pair`/`ghz_state` each spell out the produced state; `qft_circuit` gets a one-line restatement and never documents `n_qubits` or that the trailing `swap` loop reverses qubit order (bit-reversal). Bring it to parity. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/circuits/common.py:31,38-39`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Cleaner code / Performance]** DONE 2026-06-30 (P1, PR pending — migrated the bell/ghz/qft execution tests to the `run_local` fixture, hoisted `from collections import Counter`, renamed the loop var to `count`, right-sized the QFT-uniformity test to 2000 shots with `len(counts)==8` + a `>150` per-bin check) — `tests/test_circuits.py` hygiene — three tests build their own `LocalSimulator()` instead of the existing session-scoped `local_simulator`/`run_local` fixtures (`conftest.py:10-13,49-56`) that sibling tests already use; `Counter` is imported mid-function; the QFT loop var `state` actually holds an integer count; and the QFT run uses 8000 shots for a `>500` check (~16σ margin). Migrate to the fixtures, hoist the import, rename to `count`, right-size shots. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`tests/test_circuits.py:9,24,42,46,49`) — added 2026-06-29

- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-29 (QNode encoding → `features[..., i]` so it broadcasts; `train_vqc` evaluates the whole dataset in one batched call on `default.qubit`/`lightning.qubit`, keeping the per-sample loop as the documented fallback for `braket.local.qubit`. ### 25. Utilities
- [x] **[Cleaner code / Resilience]** DONE 2026-06-29 (PR pending — the "(local execution)" label now fires only when the provider's pricing is the local one (`per_minute == 0.0`); SV1 at 0 minutes is no longer mislabeled — test added) — `format_cost_warning` hardcodes "(local execution)" for every zero-cost result — `estimate_cost("SV1", estimated_minutes=0)` is `0.0`, so a genuinely billable managed simulator prints `[SV1] No cost (local execution)` (a cost-honesty mislabel in the one tool whose job is cost honesty). Gate the parenthetical on `provider == "LocalSimulator"` or use neutral "$0.00" phrasing; add the SV1-zero-minutes test. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/utils/cost.py:36-37`, `tests/test_cost.py:58-60`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Security]** DONE 2026-06-29 (PR pending — added `math.isfinite` guards for `shots` and `estimated_minutes`; NaN/inf now raise a clear ValueError before any cost is computed — tests added) — `estimate_cost` rejects negatives but lets NaN/inf silently pass the spend gate — `nan < 0` / `inf < 0` are both False, so the guards don't fire and the function returns `nan`/`inf`; a downstream `cost > budget` check against `nan` is always False, silently passing the very gate the validation protects. Extend the guards with `math.isfinite(...)` + parallel tests. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/utils/cost.py:21-24,27-29`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-29 (PR pending — guards `total_shots == 0` with a clear ValueError; tests cover both the empty `Counter` and a zero-total `Counter`) — `expectation_from_counts` has no zero-shot guard — an empty `Counter` (exactly what `parse_counts` returns for a zero-shot result) skips the loop and returns a confident `0.0` for an undefined distribution; a zero-total `Counter` raises a bare `ZeroDivisionError`. Guard `total_shots == 0` with a clear `ValueError` + tests for both. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/utils/results.py:34-38`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-29 (PR pending — raises a clear ValueError on empty/zero-total counts; tests added for both) — `plot_histogram` silently renders a blank figure on empty counts and `ZeroDivisionError`s on zero-total counts — both uncovered. Guard the empty/zero-total case (clear `ValueError` or explicit empty-state) + add tests. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/utils/visualization.py:13-14`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-29 (PR pending — added `test_parse_counts_empty_measurements_is_empty_counter` pinning the guard; it also protects the 25.f rewrite) — `parse_counts`' deliberate empty-measurements guard (`n = len(measurements[0]) if len(measurements) else 0`, the zero-shot path) is never exercised — a refactor dropping it would reintroduce an `IndexError` with no failing test. Add `parse_counts(mock_result_factory([])) == Counter()` (the conftest factory already supports `[]`). One of the parse_counts "remaining sub-items" flagged 2026-06-17. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/utils/results.py:16`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-29 (PR pending — one `np.asarray(measurements).tolist()` feeding `Counter("".join(map(str, row)) ...)`; both existing guards preserved. Verified on the browser path: `test_notebook_contract.py` (66 notebooks under qcsim) green) — `parse_counts` builds bitstrings with a nested Python generator calling `str()` on every numpy scalar (boxing each as `np.int64`) — convert once via `np.asarray(measurements).tolist()` (also transparently supports the list-based test mocks) then `"".join(map(str, row))`, preserving the `measured_qubits` guard. Use a straight `per_minute` return; make any defensive guard for a malformed entry explicit. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/utils/cost.py:26-30`) — added 2026-06-29
