### Cross-cutting (Category E): library-wide conventions
- [x] **[Consistency with existing patterns]** DONE 2026-06-30 (P1, PR pending — added fail-loud `ValueError` guards: non-empty-1D for `angle_encoding`/`iqp_encoding` (shape only — no non-negativity/power-of-2), shape checks for `hardware_efficient_ansatz` and `build_vqc_circuit` (+ `features` length >= `n_qubits`); flipped `test_classifiers.py` IndexError→ValueError and added guard tests in test_feature_maps/test_ansatz. Closes 22.c.) — The lib-wide "fail-loud `ValueError(… got {actual})`" convention is followed by 5 functions (`cost.py:21-24`, `devices.py:74-77`, `results.py:18-22`, `ansatz.py:62-66`, `feature_maps.py:82-93`) but skipped by `angle_encoding`/`iqp_encoding` (no validation) and `hardware_efficient_ansatz`/`build_vqc_circuit` (raw `IndexError`) — one test even codifies the divergence (`test_classifiers.py:26-28` asserts `IndexError`). Add the same up-front guards (non-empty 1-D for the encoders — *not* non-negativity, which is `amplitude_encoding`-specific; shape checks for the builders) and flip that test to `ValueError`. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`feature_maps.py:7-54`, `ansatz.py:7-30`, `classifiers.py:46-49`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Architecture & maintainability]** DONE 2026-06-30 (P1, PR pending — `quantum_kernel` routes through `run_circuit(device_name="local")` + `parse_counts`. Required decoupling `lib/hardware/devices.py` from `braket.aws` (lazy import via module `__getattr__`) so `lib.ml` stays importable under qcsim — verified by the browser-runnable notebook contract + a braket.aws-blocked import probe) — `ml/classifiers` bypasses both abstraction seams the library defines — it imports `LocalSimulator` directly (instead of `get_device`/`run_circuit`) and reads `result.measurement_counts` directly (instead of `parse_counts`, which has **zero** in-lib callers despite being the validated extractor). Route `quantum_kernel` through `get_device('local')` + `parse_counts` so the documented seams are real. (No latent correctness bug — the all-qubit measurement makes the guard a no-op here — purely DRY/single-source.) Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`lib/ml/classifiers.py:19,74,82,85`, `lib/utils/results.py:6-22`) — added 2026-06-29
- [x] **[Consistency with existing patterns]** DONE 2026-06-30 (P1, PR pending — added `Raises: ImportError` docstrings to `train_vqc`, `build_h2_hamiltonian`, `build_lih_hamiltonian` (train_vqc also documents its `ValueError`)) — The `Raises: ImportError` contract for lazy-`[full]`-import functions is documented on `vqc_qnode` but omitted from `train_vqc`, `build_h2_hamiltonian`, and `build_lih_hamiltonian`, which raise the same way when the extra is absent (the reason the tests `importorskip`). ### 27. Notebook curriculum — exercise loop (analyzed 2026-07-17)

> Ground truth (3-agent pass, 2026-07-17): all 44 notebooks have an exercise section — 88
> `# Exercise N:` scaffolds + 70 `TODO` code cells across 32 notebooks; prereqs use `Q1/Q2/Q3`
> self-checks with visible appended solutions; sections 01–06 explicitly withhold solutions.
> Exactly 9 static `# Hint:` lines exist curriculum-wide; there is no progressive-hint
> mechanism, no `<details>` blocks, no separate solution files. 133 `assert` statements exist
> — every one in a teaching cell, zero in exercise cells. No `check_`/`verify_`/`grade_`
> helper exists in `lib/` or `qcsim/`. Any added cell in the 32 runnable notebooks must pass
> the AST denylist + headless qcsim execution (`scripts/validate_runnable.py`,
> `tests/test_notebook_contract.py`).

- [x] **[UX]** CLOSED 2026-07-17 (PR #165, 83b8570) — **Exercise scaffolds swing between giving the answer away and giving nothing — normalize to a steer-don't-solve progressive-hint convention** — Style-A TODO scaffolds sometimes contain the full answer as commented pseudo-code (`02-hardware/notebooks/01-device-discovery.ipynb` cell 13 spells out the complete decision table the exercise asks the learner to write), while Style-B scaffolds withhold everything (`03-algorithms/notebooks/03-qft.ipynb` cell 16: "No solutions are given"; `04-quantum-ml/notebooks/02-quantum-kernels.ipynb` cell 14: "No solutions are provided."). Rework all 88 scaffolds to one convention: a goal statement + expected-output shape in the code cell, with tiered collapsible hints (`<details><summary>Hint 1 — nudge</summary>` then `Hint 2 — approach`) in the adjacent markdown cell — Jupyter renders `<details>` natively, and markdown-only edits cannot break the runnable contract. Answer-revealing pseudo-code moves into the deepest hint tier; barren scaffolds gain the first two tiers. Impact: High. Effort: High. (`02-hardware/notebooks/01-device-discovery.ipynb` cell 13, `03-algorithms/notebooks/03-qft.ipynb` cell 16, 9 `# Hint:` lines total across 9 notebooks) — added 2026-07-17
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** CLOSED 2026-07-17 (PR #165, 83b8570) — **"The asserts you write are your answer key" is a promise the notebooks never keep — make the answer key executable** — `03-algorithms/notebooks/02-grovers-search.ipynb` cell 16 tells learners their asserts are the answer key, but every assert in an exercise scaffold is commented out (cell 17), and all 133 live asserts sit in teaching cells: a learner finishing an exercise has no way to know they got it right. Add a "Check your work" code cell per exercise that asserts properties of the learner's result (e.g. GHZ-5: counts contain only `00000`/`11111`) without revealing construction — property checks run identically under real Braket and qcsim via the existing `statevector()` helper, and the runnable-contract CI (headless execution of every cell) will exercise them forever. Flagged: the minimal new surface is a small browser-safe check-helper module (house precedent: `lib/utils/statevector.py`, added for exactly this dual-runtime reason); checks referencing learner-defined variables must no-op with a "not attempted yet" message when the TODO variables are absent, so unsolved exercises don't fail CI. Impact: High. Effort: High. (`03-algorithms/notebooks/02-grovers-search.ipynb` cells 16-17, `lib/utils/statevector.py:29`, `scripts/validate_runnable.py:69-102`) — added 2026-07-17
- [x] **[Consistency]** CLOSED 2026-07-17 (PR #165, 83b8570) — **Three exercise idioms coexist** — `## Exercises` (32 notebooks) vs numbered `## N. Exercises` (6) vs `## N. Self-check` (6 prereqs); `# Exercise N:` scaffolds vs prereq `Q1/Q2/Q3` cells; literal `TODO` in 32 notebooks but absent from the 9 Style-B notebooks. One idiom (fold into the hint-convention pass above) makes the format learnable and machine-checkable — a contract test can then assert every exercise cell carries the convention, the same way the manifest drift-gate works. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low (if folded into the scaffold pass). (`00-prereqs/notebooks/01-python-numpy-warmup.ipynb` cell 13 vs `01-foundations/notebooks/01-first-circuit.ipynb` cell 12 vs `03-algorithms/notebooks/02-grovers-search.ipynb` cell 17) — added 2026-07-17

### 34. Quantum Workspace authentication
- [x] **[Accessibility]** DONE 2026-06-28 (unit-verified: focus moves to the step <h1> on view change via a prevView guard that skips mount + StrictMode double-invoke) — Multi-step view switches lose focus and announce nothing to screen readers — AuthForm swaps the entire form in place when the flow advances (sign-up -> confirm, forgot -> reset, reset -> sign-in) by calling setView, but nothing manages focus or announces the change. On a successful transition the element that had focus (the just-clicked submit button) is unmounted, so focus falls back to <body>; keyboard users land nowhere and must re-tab from the top, and screen-reader users get no notice that a new step appeared. The heading text updates but the <h1> is neither focused nor a live region, so the change is silent on the success path (only the error path emits the role=alert). Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:81` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:89` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:113-118` · `web/src/app/layout.tsx:41`) — added 2026-06-28
- [x] **[Accessibility]** DONE 2026-06-28 (rebuilt as a full WAI-APG menu button: role=menu/menuitem, roving tabindex, Arrow/Home/End, Enter/Space activation, Escape returns focus to trigger, Tab-out closes via focusout; unit-verified) — Account-menu dropdown does not return focus to its trigger on Escape, and promises menu semantics it never provides — AccountMenu opens a popup whose trigger declares aria-haspopup="true" (i.e. a menu), but the popup <div> has no role="menu" and its children are a plain Link and button with no role="menuitem" or arrow-key navigation. More concretely, the Escape handler only calls setOpen(false); if the user had tabbed into the Workspace link or Sign out button, closing unmounts those elements and focus is dropped to <body> instead of returning to the trigger, breaking the WAI menu-button keyboard contract. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/account-menu.tsx:14-15` · `web/src/components/auth/account-menu.tsx:47` · `web/src/components/auth/account-menu.tsx:57-78`) — added 2026-06-28
- [x] **[Accessibility & consistency]** DONE 2026-06-28 (LiveStatus extracted to components/live-status.tsx + re-exported from widget-ui; checklist announces the gating milestone on sign-up/reset via the shared idiom + shared allCriteriaMet) — Password checklist gives no live announcement (bypasses shared LiveStatus idiom) — PasswordChecklist renders a plain <ul> with no role or aria-live, so when a rule flips from not-met to met as the user types, screen readers say nothing. Each <li> does carry an aria-label conveying met/not-met (so pass/fail is correctly conveyed by more than color and icon when navigated to), and the input's aria-describedby reads the list once on focus — but there is no feedback during typing without re-focusing. The component is also conditionally mounted (rendered only once `password` is truthy), so an aria-live region placed inside it would miss its own first render. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/password-checklist.tsx:40` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:136` · `web/src/components/quantum/widget-ui.tsx:238-244` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:134,136`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Cleaner code]** Duplicated new-password entry block across signUp and reset views — The signUp and reset views each render the same trio — a primary PasswordField, a 'confirm' PasswordField, and a conditional PasswordChecklist with confirm matching — differing only in id prefixes and which password state they bind. The validity gate is likewise duplicated as two parallel expressions. Any change to the password-entry UX (autoComplete, a new rule, the match check) must be made in two places that can silently drift. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. - [x] **[Performance]** DONE 2026-06-28 (moved the SDK into a next/dynamic({ssr:false}) AmplifyAuthBridge; provider is now Amplify-free. Build-proof: the ~90KB Amplify chunk is absent from every non-auth page's HTML — only /login pulls it. Live-verified sign-in/out still work) — aws-amplify v6 sits in the global shared chunk, loaded (and parsed) on all 107 pages, not just auth routes — auth-provider.tsx statically imports aws-amplify, aws-amplify/utils, and aws-amplify/auth at module top level. That module is pulled into every page two ways: layout.tsx mounts <AuthProvider> wrapping all routes, and nav.tsx -> account-menu.tsx imports useAuth from the same module. - [x] **[Resilience & UX]** DONE 2026-06-28 (unit-verified: guarded async handler with 30s cooldown + countdown, role="status" feedback, mapped-error surfacing, double-click guard) — Resend-code button: unhandled rejection, no cooldown, no feedback — The standalone resend handler fires the network call as a floating promise with no catch, so any rejection (Cognito LimitExceededException, network failure) becomes an unhandled promise rejection. The button is never disabled and has no cooldown, so a user who doesn't see an email can rapid-click it straight into a rate-limit, and there is no success or error feedback at all — a silent failure on a step every email signup depends on. The error-mapper already has friendly copy for the very LimitExceeded case this triggers, but resend never routes through it. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:98-100` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:192-196` · `web/src/lib/auth-errors.ts:39-41` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:98`) — added 2026-06-28
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-28 (live-verified: 15s timeout bounced /auth/callback → /login?error=google) — Callback page can hang forever on a missed redirect-failure event — The callback page's only escape on a failed Google token exchange is catching the ephemeral `signInWithRedirect_failure` Hub event; it has no terminal handling for an `unauthenticated` status. Hub events are not buffered or replayed for late listeners, and Amplify can fire the failure during configure/initial load — before this effect's `Hub.listen` registers, or during the cleanup-then-resubscribe gap when status flips configuring→unauthenticated. If that event is missed, status settles on `unauthenticated`, no further event arrives, and the user is stranded on "Signing you in…" with no recovery. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/auth/callback/page.tsx:12-30` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:71-82` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:49-59`) — added 2026-06-28
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-28 (unit-verified: tokenRefresh_failure/redirect_failure now clear state; useRef sequence guard tested against the hydrate-after-signout race) — AuthProvider Hub listener ignores failure/refresh events and has no re-hydrate sequence guard — The provider's Hub switch handles only success and sign-out, so a `tokenRefresh_failure` (expired/revoked session) leaves the UI showing "authenticated" with a stale email indefinitely, and `signInWithRedirect_failure` is dropped. Separately, `hydrate()` is invoked from mount and from every signedIn/signInWithRedirect event with no in-flight or sequence guard, so concurrent runs are last-write-wins: a slow hydrate started by a `signedIn` can resolve after a synchronous `signedOut` and clobber the state back to authenticated. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:71-82` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:49-59,74-76` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:86-88`) — added 2026-06-28
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-28 (10 new tests added — Hub unmount cleanup, tokenRefresh_failure, hydrate/signout race, signOut-rejection settling, token storage, callback timeout, resend success/failure/double-click; full suite 760/760) — Test gaps on the exact resilience edge paths (cleanup, failure events, double-submit, resend) — The suite exercises happy paths and the auto-resend, but the resilience-critical edges are untested. The provider test declares a `hubUnsub` mock but never asserts it fires on unmount, never exercises `signInWithRedirect` or any failure/refresh event; the form test has no coverage for the manual Resend button, the double-submit `busy` guard, or a generic/network error mapping to the default message; the callback test has no missed-event/hang case; and the sign-out swallow path is only ever tested with a resolving mock. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/__tests__/components/auth/auth-provider.test.tsx:13` · `web/__tests__/components/auth/auth-form.test.tsx:94-103` · `auth-form.tsx:50` · `web/__tests__/app/auth-callback-page.test.tsx:51-55`) — added 2026-06-28
- [x] **[Security (session, OAuth, XSS)]** DONE 2026-06-28 (live-verified: from a purged clean baseline, a fresh sign-in put 0 Cognito keys in localStorage / 6 in sessionStorage, and the same-origin lab tab sees 0; fix = `cognitoUserPoolsTokenProvider.setKeyValueStorage(sessionStorage)`) — Cognito tokens persist in localStorage, reachable by the same-origin Pyodide lab tab — The app calls Amplify.configure(cfg) with no token-storage override, so aws-amplify v6 keeps the Cognito id/access/refresh tokens in the browser's localStorage by default — persistent and shared across every same-origin tab. The site also opens the JupyterLite/Pyodide lab in a new tab at the same origin (/lab/lab/index.html), where arbitrary user Python can reach JS via `import js` and read window.localStorage, i.e. the persisted 30-day refresh token. Any same-origin script execution (a malicious/pasted notebook cell, or any future XSS) can therefore exfiltrate a long-lived account credential. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:64` · `web/src/lib/auth-config.ts:37-53` · `web/src/components/notebook-link.tsx:21-23` · `/lab/lab/index.html`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[UX]** Password-reset view lacks "we emailed you a code" context, a resend/back affordance, and any success confirmation — When "Send reset code" succeeds, the user is dropped onto the reset view showing a bare "Reset code" field with no explanation that a code was emailed or to which address — unlike the confirm view, which does show that helper text. The reset view also has no "Resend code" and no "Back to sign in" link (the forgot view has the latter), so a user who never received the email is stranded. On success, confirmReset jumps straight back to the sign-in form with no "Your password was reset — please sign in" message, leaving users unsure the change took. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:185` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:214` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:91` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:206`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[UX]** Confirmation/reset code inputs miss one-time-code autofill, numeric keypad, and autofocus — The confirmation-code and reset-code inputs are rendered via the generic Field component as plain type="text" with no autoComplete, inputMode, or autofocus. On mobile this means the OS will not offer to autofill the just-emailed 6-digit code, users get the full alphabetic keyboard instead of a number pad, and after the view transition focus is not placed on the code field, forcing an extra tap/click before they can type. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:188` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:216` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:242`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Accessibility]** Password eyeball toggle double-encodes its state (aria-pressed plus a flipping label) — The show/hide button both flips its accessible name between "Show password" and "Hide password" AND toggles aria-pressed in lockstep. A screen reader therefore announces something like "Hide password, pressed" — the state is conveyed twice and the meaning of "pressed" relative to a verb-phrase label is ambiguous. WAI toggle-button guidance is to pick one mechanism: a stable name plus aria-pressed, or a state-describing name without aria-pressed. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/password-field.tsx:39` · `web/src/components/auth/password-field.tsx:40`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Architecture & maintainability]** Status-gated view boilerplate and 'coming soon' copy duplicated across three pages — login, workspace, and callback pages each independently branch on auth status and hand-roll a useEffect+router.replace redirect. The unconfigured 'The Quantum Workspace / Free accounts are coming soon.' panel is duplicated verbatim in two separate files, so a copy edit in one can silently diverge from the other. The status-to-redirect effect pattern is re-implemented three times with slightly different targets. Impact: Low. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/app/login/page.tsx:19-27` · `web/src/app/workspace/page.tsx:17-28` · `web/src/app/auth/callback/page.tsx:12-30`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Architecture & maintainability]** 288-line single-component form repeats submit-button and link scaffolding 5x — AuthForm holds all five views in one 288-line component. The cross-view shared state (email/password/code carrying between sign-up→confirm and forgot→reset) legitimately justifies keeping it as one component rather than splitting into five files, but the per-view markup is copy-pasted: five near-identical submit buttons each re-implement the busy/disabled/label pattern, and the 'back to sign in' link block is duplicated. This is the largest file in the feature and the duplication makes a styling or wording change a five-place edit. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:137-138,171-172,189-190,203-204,233-234` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:175-177,207-209` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Architecture & maintainability]** Env gate requires NEXT_PUBLIC_AWS_REGION that the runtime auth config never consumes — isAuthConfigured() returns false unless all four vars (including region) are present, gating the entire workspace/auth surface. But amplifyAuthConfig() builds the Amplify v6 config without region at all (Amplify derives it from userPoolId), and the comment admits region is collected only 'for the gate + the future sync-backend API client.' So an operator who sets the three functionally-required vars but omits region gets a fully-inert feature for a value nothing currently uses. The single-sourcing itself is good — only auth-config.ts reads these env vars — but the gate is wider than the runtime need. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/auth-config.ts:22` · `web/src/lib/auth-config.ts:37-53` · `web/src/lib/auth-config.ts:11-14`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Cleaner code]** Two divergent view-transition paths leave transient fields stale — `goTo` is documented as the safe transition that clears the confirm field and error before switching views, but the success handlers and the error path bypass it and call `setView` directly, so they clear nothing. After `doReset` returns to signIn, `confirm`, `newPassword`, and `code` all linger in state; and even `goTo` only clears `confirm`+`error`, not `code`/`newPassword`, so its own stated guarantee ('a confirm value never carries between sign-up and reset') is partial. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. - [ ] **[Cleaner code]** `confirm` state name collides with the `confirm` view and `doConfirm` handler — The `confirm` state variable holds the confirm-password value, but `"confirm"` is also an AuthView (the email-confirmation-code screen) and `doConfirm` is the handler that confirms email sign-up. Reading calls like `setConfirm("")` next to confirm-view logic invites misreading them as related to email confirmation when they only reset the confirm-password input. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. The two inputs are meant to look identical, but each carries its own copy of the long class string, so a tweak to one (border, background, focus ring) can silently desync the visual appearance of email/code inputs vs password inputs. - [ ] **[Performance]** hydrate() makes a Cognito GetUser network round-trip on every cold page load just to read the email already present in the ID token — On mount (which happens on every page, since AuthProvider lives in the root layout) hydrate() awaits getCurrentUser() and then fetchUserAttributes(). In aws-amplify v6 fetchUserAttributes() calls the Cognito GetUser API — a network request — performed on every cold load for an authenticated user solely to display their email in the Nav. The email is already available offline in the cached ID token claims, so the network hop is avoidable. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:49-59` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:61-84` · `web/src/lib/auth-config.ts:45`) — added 2026-06-28
- [x] **[Resilience & tests]** DONE 2026-06-28 (live-verified: sign-out cleared sessionStorage → 0 and showed signed-out UI; try/catch/finally always settles unauthenticated, rejection path unit-verified) — Sign-out rejection is swallowed, leaving the user apparently still signed in — `signOut` in the provider awaits Amplify with no try/catch, and both call sites invoke it as fire-and-forget. In the account menu a rejected sign-out is an unhandled rejection that updates nothing (status only changes via the `signedOut` Hub event, which won't fire on failure), so the menu closes but the user stays signed in with no error shown. On the workspace page a rejection skips the redirect home and is likewise unhandled. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/account-menu.tsx:72` · `web/src/app/workspace/page.tsx:41-44,67` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-provider.tsx:86-88`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Security & architecture]** Password policy lives in 3 hand-synced copies (checklist / policy / cognito.yaml) with no drift guard — password-policy.ts is the single source of the client-side checklist and the sign-up/reset submit gate, and its header comment states the rules MUST mirror the pool's PasswordPolicy and must be kept in sync 'by hand'. They are in exact parity today, but nothing enforces it: there is no test that reads cognito.yaml. If the pool policy is later tightened (e.g. RequireSymbols flipped on) without editing password-policy.ts, the checklist would tell users a too-weak password is valid and the submit button would enable, producing confusing InvalidPasswordException failures the client said could not happen. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/password-policy.ts:1-4` · `web/src/lib/password-policy.ts:20-25` · `infra/workspace/cognito.yaml:44-49` · `web/__tests__/lib/password-policy.test.ts`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Security (authz, env, Cognito config)]** Production Cognito app client allow-lists http://localhost:3000 redirect URLs — The single app client that backs production quantum.altivum.ai lists both the HTTPS prod origin AND http://localhost:3000 in its OAuth CallbackURLs and LogoutURLs. Shipping a non-TLS localhost redirect target inside a production identity provider's allow-list is a least-privilege / defense-in-depth violation: it widens the set of origins that can complete an OAuth flow against the live user pool (e.g. any local app or malware bound to port 3000 leveraging an existing hosted-UI SSO session). The authorization-code + public-client + PKCE setup (responseType code, GenerateSecret false) mitigates classic code interception, but the localhost entries should not exist in the production client at all. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`infra/workspace/cognito.yaml:98-100` · `infra/workspace/cognito.yaml:101-103` · `infra/workspace/cognito.yaml:83` · `web/src/lib/auth-config.ts:46-48`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Security (authz, env, Cognito config)]** User pool has no advanced-security / threat-protection add-on on a public self-signup endpoint — The user pool enables open self-signup (AllowAdminCreateUserOnly false) over the public SRP flow but defines no UserPoolAddOns block, so AdvancedSecurityMode defaults to OFF. There is no compromised-credentials (breached-password) blocking or adaptive/risk-based detection on the publicly reachable sign-in/sign-up endpoints. Note this is a deliberate-tradeoff candidate: the account stores only an email and device-local lesson progress with no backend secrets, and Cognito threat protection is a paid tier in a cost-conscious project — so the honest call may be to decline it; it is flagged for completeness on this lens. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`infra/workspace/cognito.yaml:28-61` · `infra/workspace/cognito.yaml:41-42` · `infra/workspace/cognito.yaml:84-85`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[UX]** Error banner is not focus-managed and inputs stay live during in-flight requests — The error message renders at the top of the form with role="alert" (announced to screen readers) but focus is never moved to it and it is not scrolled into view, so on the taller sign-up/reset forms a sighted keyboard user who just pressed a submit button at the bottom may not notice the new error above the fold. Additionally, the text Field inputs and the "Continue with Google" button are never disabled while busy, so a user can edit the email/password or kick off a Google redirect mid-request. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:119` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:260` · `web/src/components/auth/auth-form.tsx:279`) — added 2026-06-28

### 35. Glossary
- [ ] **[Performance]** Glossary entries aren't memoized — every keystroke re-runs the full react-markdown + KaTeX pipeline for each matched term — The Glossary index maps each filtered term to a <GlossaryEntry>, which renders an <InlineMarkdown> wrapping react-markdown with remark-math + rehype-katex. Neither GlossaryEntry nor InlineMarkdown is wrapped in React.memo, and react-markdown's default synchronous component does NO internal caching — it rebuilds a fresh unified() processor and re-runs parse + KaTeX rendering on every render. So on every keystroke in the search box, the Glossary state change re-renders every still-mounted matched entry, and each one re-parses its LaTeX and rebuilds KaTeX DOM from scratch — pure wasted work because the definition strings never change. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/glossary/glossary.tsx:63-77` · `web/src/components/glossary/glossary-entry.tsx:9-32` · `web/src/components/glossary/inline-markdown.tsx:15-25` · `node_modules/react-markdown/lib/index.js:175-178`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Performance]** ~89 KaTeX definitions render on the client at hydration despite being fully static at build time — Both Glossary and InlineMarkdown are client components ("use client"), so on the static-export index page the entire react-markdown → remark-math → rehype-katex pipeline executes in the browser during hydration for all ~89 entries at once (roughly 150-250 KaTeX expressions), blocking the main thread on first interaction. Every definition is a constant string known at build time, and the project already builds with output:"export", so this rendering can happen at build instead of in every visitor's browser. It also forces react-markdown, remark-math and rehype-katex into the index page's client JS bundle. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/components/glossary/inline-markdown.tsx:1` · `web/src/components/glossary/glossary.tsx:1` · `web/src/components/glossary/glossary-entry.tsx:26-28` · `web/src/app/glossary/page.tsx:11-30`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[SEO]** No DefinedTerm / DefinedTermSet JSON-LD on glossary pages — The term pages emit only title, description, canonical, OpenGraph and Twitter via the Metadata API and render no structured data; a repo-wide grep for `application/ld+json` returns zero hits. A glossary is the textbook use case for schema.org `DefinedTerm` (per entry) inside a `DefinedTermSet` (the index), which is exactly the structured data Google rich-results and AI/GEO answer engines look for to understand definitional content. Absent it, the 89 term pages are just prose to a crawler. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:29-35` · `web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:43-50`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[SEO]** Glossary index page is missing canonical, OpenGraph and Twitter tags — The /glossary index — the primary, most-linked entry point of the feature — sets only title and description. It declares no `alternates.canonical` (so Next emits no <link rel="canonical"> for it at all) and no openGraph/twitter blocks, while every per-term page does set all three. The most shareable glossary URL therefore unfurls as a bare link and has no self-referential canonical. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/glossary/page.tsx:5-9` · `web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:32-34`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[SEO]** Meta descriptions are grammatically broken where inline math/code is stripped — Per-term descriptions are built as `truncateAtWord(plainText(term.definition), 155)`. plainText replaces every `$math$` and `` `code` `` span with a single space, which leaves a space before the following punctuation and a dangling connector when the math is mid-sentence. For Bell pair the SERP/social description becomes "...maximally entangled state such as ; measuring one fixes the other's outcome." — a stray space before the semicolon and a dropped clause. This degrades the snippet on many of the math-heavy entries. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. (`web/src/lib/glossary.ts:73-79` · `web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:27` · `web/src/lib/glossary.ts:99`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[SEO]** No OpenGraph/Twitter image and a context-free one-word OG title — Term pages set openGraph and twitter but supply no `images`, and `twitter.card` is `summary` (no large image). The site ships no OG asset at all (public/ has only lab/ and pyodide/). The OG title is also the bare term — `openGraph: { title: term.term }` yields "Amplitude" — so a shared link gives no product context and no visual, which weakens click-through from social and AI surfaces that preview cards. Impact: Medium. Effort: Medium. (`web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:33-34`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[UI]** "See also" + Workspace-CTA muted text bypasses the .text-caption tier (fails AA in dark mode) — The glossary hand-rolls its muted/footnote text instead of the single-source .text-caption utility that the design system created precisely to keep that tier WCAG-AA in both themes. SeeAlsoLinks sets `text-xs text-gray-500` with no dark: variant, so in dark mode the "See also:" label and separators stay gray-500 on the dark card (~4.15:1, below the 4.5:1 AA floor for small text). WorkspaceCta's disabled teaser uses `text-gray-400 dark:text-gray-500` — the exact inverted, sub-AA literal that globals.css says .text-caption was introduced to replace — and the empty-state re-types the correct pair by hand, so three muted treatments coexist in one feature. - [ ] **[Accessibility]** Glossary search box is not exposed as a search landmark — The glossary's primary control is a properly-labelled search input, but it sits inside a plain sticky <div> with no role="search" (or native <search>) wrapper. Activating a letter scrolls the viewport but, because the target is not a focusable element, keyboard focus does not land in the chosen section and relies entirely on browsers' default fragment focus-starting-point behavior — which the project itself does not trust elsewhere, having added `tabIndex={-1}` to the <main> skip-link target. - [ ] **[Consistency & resilience]** CopyLinkButton forks the shared CopyButton (weaker: silent failure, no insecure-context fallback) — CopyLinkButton uses only `navigator.clipboard.writeText` and, on rejection, runs an empty catch ("no-op") — so in an insecure context or older browser the click does nothing with zero feedback, and the button still reads "Copy link". - [ ] **[Performance]** matchesQuery re-normalizes every term's static text on each keystroke — On each keystroke the filter calls matchesQuery for all 89 terms, and matchesQuery rebuilds the haystack from term + aliases + plainText(definition) and runs normalize() (NFD + diacritic regex + toLowerCase) plus plainText's three regex passes over that static text every single time. When a query matches nothing, the empty state is a single static sentence with no way to reset; the user must manually select-and-delete the input to recover. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/glossary/glossary.tsx:21-29` · `web/src/components/glossary/glossary.tsx:58-61`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[UX]** "All terms" back link drops the user at the top of the index, losing their place — From a term detail page, the "All terms" link targets `/glossary` (top of the index), so returning a reader to the entry they just clicked requires scrolling/searching again. Each index entry already exposes a stable anchor id (`termSlug`), so the link could return the user directly to that entry. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/glossary/term-detail.tsx:14-22` · `web/src/components/glossary/glossary-entry.tsx:12-13`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[UX]** "Sign-up coming soon" renders as a button-shaped but inert element — When auth is not configured, the Workspace CTA renders a `<span>` styled with a border, padding, and control radius — visually identical to a clickable button — but it is non-interactive and carries no disabled semantics. Users may try to click it and get no response, with no indication it is intentionally inert. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/components/glossary/workspace-cta.tsx:26-29` · `web/src/components/glossary/workspace-cta.tsx:19-24`) — added 2026-06-28

### 36. Sitemap & robots (SEO)
- [ ] **[Architecture & maintainability]** Route-path construction is duplicated across sitemap and pages instead of single-sourced — The URL path scheme for terms and lessons is rebuilt inline in the sitemap and again independently in each dynamic page. sitemap.ts constructs `/glossary/${termSlug(t.term)}` and `/learn/${s.slug}` by hand, while the term page rebuilds the identical `/glossary/${termSlug(term.term)}` for its canonical/OG metadata, and each page's generateStaticParams maps the same source arrays. There is no shared `termPath()`/`sectionPath()` helper, so the path scheme lives in three+ places that must be edited in lockstep. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/sitemap.ts:10` · `web/src/app/sitemap.ts:11` · `web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:28` · `web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:20`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[Consistency with existing patterns]** Hardcoded static-route triple lacks the single-source documentation used everywhere else — The static public routes are a bare literal `["", "/glossary", "/review"]` with no comment explaining why /login, /workspace, and /auth/callback are intentionally excluded, or that the list must be updated by hand when a public top-level page is added. Every other route/URL source in the codebase (site.ts, sections.ts, manifest.ts) carries an explicit single-source comment; this is the one relisted route list and the only place with no such note, making it the easiest spot to drift. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/sitemap.ts:9` · `web/src/lib/site.ts:1-2` · `web/src/lib/sections.ts:11-13`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[SEO]** Canonical tags are set on term pages but missing on the other sitemap-listed pages — metadataBase is correctly set in layout.tsx, and the per-term pages emit an absolute canonical via `alternates: { canonical: url }`. But the other URLs the sitemap advertises — home (/), /glossary, /review, and every /learn/{section} — never set `alternates.canonical`, and Next does not auto-emit a canonical link from metadataBase alone. The result is an inconsistency: the sitemap lists these pages but they ship no self-referencing canonical, unlike their term-page siblings, leaving query-param or trailing-slash variants without an explicit canonical signal. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/glossary/[term]/page.tsx:32` · `web/src/app/layout.tsx:23` · `web/src/app/glossary/page.tsx:5` · `web/src/app/review/page.tsx:5`) — added 2026-06-28
- [ ] **[SEO & correctness]** robots.txt does not Disallow the thin/auth routes the sitemap deliberately excludes — The sitemap deliberately omits the auth routes (/login, /workspace, /auth/callback) and the JupyterLite /lab app, but robots.ts emits only `allow: "/"` with no `disallow`, and none of the statically-exported auth shells carry a `noindex` meta. So the two halves of this one feature disagree: the sitemap says "don't surface these," while robots.txt actively invites crawlers into them. In production (where `isAuthConfigured()` is true, per the 4 Cognito vars in Amplify) the nav "Sign in" link and the glossary "Sign up free" CTA make /login reachable from crawled pages, and /lab exposes ~680 crawlable JupyterLite internal files — so the index can fill with thin auth shells and app-internal JSON. Impact: Low. Effort: Low. (`web/src/app/robots.ts:8` · `web/src/app/sitemap.ts:9` · `web/src/components/auth/account-menu.tsx:34-35` · `web/src/components/glossary/workspace-cta.tsx:21`) — added 2026-06-28

### 37. Graded Rep widgets & mastery loop
- [x] **[Consistency]** CLOSED 2026-07-17 (PR #166, ac1db0e) — **Solved-state persistence is asymmetric across the six Rep kinds** — `challenge` and `debug` write a set-once solved flag (`qc:challenge:<id>` at `challenge.tsx:39,93-95`; `qc:debug:<id>` at `debug-circuit-widget.tsx:41,90`), but `predict`/`bloch`/`cost`/`expect` persist only FSRS card state (`predict-widget.tsx:130`, `bloch-target-widget.tsx:151`, `cost-estimate-widget.tsx:125`, `expectation-widget.tsx:118`), so any surface counting "solved" outcomes undercounts four of six kinds, and the synced snapshot carries an inconsistent record shape per kind. Either write the flag in all six widgets or derive "solved" uniformly from card state everywhere and retire the two flags. Impact: Medium. Effort: Low. — added 2026-07-17
